Park](Butrint_National_Park "Butrint National Park"){.wikilink},
occupying a peninsula surrounded by the Lake of Butrint and the [Channel
of Vivari](Channel_of_Vivari "Channel of Vivari"){.wikilink}. In the
west, stretching along the [Albanian Adriatic Sea
Coast](Albanian_Adriatic_Sea_Coast "Albanian Adriatic Sea Coast"){.wikilink},
the [Divjakë-Karavasta National
Park](Divjakë-Karavasta_National_Park "Divjakë-Karavasta National Park"){.wikilink}
boasts the extensive [Lagoon of
Karavasta](Lagoon_of_Karavasta "Lagoon of Karavasta"){.wikilink}, one of
the largest lagoon systems in the Mediterranean Sea. Notably, Europe\'s
first wild river national park, [Vjosa National
Park](Vjosa_Wild_River_National_Park "Vjosa National Park"){.wikilink},
safeguards the [Vjosa River](Vjosa "Vjosa River"){.wikilink} and its
primary tributaries, which originates in the
[Pindus](Pindus "Pindus"){.wikilink} Mountains and flows to the Adriatic
Sea. [Dajti Mountain National
Park](Dajti_Mountain_National_Park "Dajti Mountain National Park"){.wikilink},
[Lurë-Dejë Mountain National
Park](Lurë-Dejë_Mountain_National_Park "Lurë-Dejë Mountain National Park"){.wikilink}
and [Tomorr Mountain National
Park](Tomorr_Mountain_National_Park "Tomorr Mountain National Park"){.wikilink}
protect the mountainous terrain of the centre of Albania, including the
[Tomorr](Tomorr "Tomorr"){.wikilink} and [Skanderbeg
Mountains](Skanderbeg_Mountains "Skanderbeg Mountains"){.wikilink}.

### Environmental issues {#environmental_issues}

```{=mediawiki}
{{Main|Environmental issues in Albania}}
```
Environmental issues in Albania notably encompass
[air](Air_pollution "air"){.wikilink} and [water
pollution](water_pollution "water pollution"){.wikilink}, [climate
change](Climate_change_in_Albania "climate change"){.wikilink} impacts,
[waste management](waste_management "waste management"){.wikilink}
shortcomings, [biodiversity
loss](Conservation_biology "biodiversity loss"){.wikilink} and
imperative for [nature
conservation](nature_conservation "nature conservation"){.wikilink}.[^190][^191]

Climate change is predicted to exert significant impacts on the quality
of life in Albania.[^192] Albania is one of the European countries most
at risk and vulnerable to [natural
disasters](Natural_disaster "natural disasters"){.wikilink}.[^193]
Natural disasters, such as [floods](Flood "floods"){.wikilink}, [forest
fires](Wildfire "forest fires"){.wikilink}, and
[landslides](Landslide "landslides"){.wikilink}, are increasing in
Albania due to climate change, causing significant damage.[^194][^195]
Rising sea levels are anticipated to negatively impact coastal
communities and the tourism industry.[^196]

In 2023 Albania emitted 7.67 million tonnes of [greenhouse
gases](Greenhouse_gas "greenhouse gases"){.wikilink},[^197] equivalent
to 2.73 tonnes per person,[^198] making it a relatively low emitting
country. Albania has pledged a 20.9% reduction in GHG emissions by 2030,
and [net zero](Net-zero_emissions "net zero"){.wikilink} by 2050.[^199]

The country has a moderate and improving performance in the
[Environmental Performance
Index](Environmental_Performance_Index "Environmental Performance Index"){.wikilink}
with an overall ranking of 62 out of 180 countries in 2022.[^200]
However, Albania\'s ranking has decreased since its highest placement at
position 15 in the Environmental Performance Index of 2012.[^201]

```{=mediawiki}
{{Panorama |image=Prespa_and_Prespa_National_Park_Albania_2017.jpg |height=210px |caption={{Center|The [[Prespa National Park (Albania)|Prespa National Park]] in southeastern Albania is part of the [[European Green Belt]] and [[Ohrid-Prespa Transboundary Biosphere Reserve|Ohrid-Prespa Biosphere Reserve]].}}}}
```
## Politics

```{=mediawiki}
{{Main|Politics of Albania}}
```
```{=mediawiki}
{{See also|Government of Albania}}
```
+----------------------------------+----------------------------------+
| ![](Bajram_Begaj_(i              | ![](Edi                          |
| nfobox_crop).jpg "Bajram_Begaj_( | _Rama_(2024-02-29).jpg "Edi_Rama |
| infobox_crop).jpg"){width="108"} | _(2024-02-29).jpg"){width="120"} |
+----------------------------------+----------------------------------+
| [Bajram                          | [Edi                             |
| Begaj](Bajram_B                  | Rama](                           |
| egaj "Bajram Begaj"){.wikilink}\ | Edi_Rama "Edi Rama"){.wikilink}\ |
| `{{Small|[[President of Al       | `{{S                             |
| bania|President]]}}`{=mediawiki} | mall|[[Prime Minister of Albania |
|                                  | |Prime Minister]]}}`{=mediawiki} |
+----------------------------------+----------------------------------+

Since declaring independence in 1912, Albania has experienced a
significant political transformation, traversing through distinct
periods that included a monarchical rule, a communist regime and the
eventual establishment of a democratic order.[^202] In 1998, Albania
transitioned into a [sovereign](sovereign_state "sovereign"){.wikilink}
[parliamentary](parliamentary_republic "parliamentary"){.wikilink}
[constitutional
republic](constitutional_republic "constitutional republic"){.wikilink},
marking a fundamental milestone in its political evolution.[^203] Its
governance structure operates under a
[constitution](Constitution_of_Albania "constitution"){.wikilink} that
serves as the principal document of the country.[^204] The constitution
is grounded in the principle of the [separation of
powers](separation_of_powers "separation of powers"){.wikilink}, with
three arms of government that encompass the legislative embodied in the
[Parliament](Parliament_of_Albania "Parliament"){.wikilink}, the
executive led by the
[President](President_of_Albania "President"){.wikilink} as the
ceremonial [head of state](head_of_state "head of state"){.wikilink} and
the [Prime
Minister](Prime_Minister_of_Albania "Prime Minister"){.wikilink} as the
functional [head of
government](head_of_government "head of government"){.wikilink}, and the
judiciary with a hierarchy of courts, including the
[constitutional](Constitutional_Court_of_Albania "constitutional"){.wikilink}
and [supreme
courts](Supreme_Court_of_Albania "supreme courts"){.wikilink} as well as
multiple [appeal](Appeals_courts_of_Albania "appeal"){.wikilink} and
[administrative
courts](Administrative_Courts_in_Albania "administrative courts"){.wikilink}.[^205]

Albania\'s legal system is structured to protect its people\'s political
rights, regardless of their ethnic, linguistic, racial, or religious
affiliations.[^206][^207] Despite these principles, there are
significant human rights concerns in Albania that demand
attention.[^208] These concerns include issues related to the
independence of the judiciary, the absence of a free media sector and
the enduring problem of corruption within various governmental bodies,
law enforcement agencies and other institutions.[^209] As Albania
pursues its path towards EU membership, active efforts are being made to
achieve substantial improvements in these areas to align with EU
criteria and standards.[^210]

### Foreign relations {#foreign_relations}

```{=mediawiki}
{{Main|Foreign relations of Albania}}
```
![Assisted by the governments of [Kosovo](Kosovo "Kosovo"){.wikilink}
and Albania, an official application for the inclusion of the [Arbëreshë
people](Arbëreshë_people "Arbëreshë people"){.wikilink} in the list of
[UNESCO](UNESCO "UNESCO"){.wikilink}\'s [Intangible Cultural
Heritage](UNESCO_Intangible_Cultural_Heritage_Lists "Intangible Cultural Heritage"){.wikilink}
is being
prepared.[^211]](Artigianato_Arberesh.jpg "Assisted by the governments of Kosovo and Albania, an official application for the inclusion of the Arbëreshë people in the list of UNESCO's Intangible Cultural Heritage is being prepared.")

Emerging from decades of isolation during the communism, Albania has
adopted a [foreign
policy](Foreign_relations_of_Albania "foreign policy"){.wikilink}
orientation centred on active cooperation and engagement in
international affairs. At the core of Albania\'s foreign policies lie a
set of objectives, which encompass the commitment to protect its
sovereignty and territorial integrity, the cultivation of diplomatic
ties with other countries, advocating for [international recognition of
Kosovo](international_recognition_of_Kosovo "international recognition of Kosovo"){.wikilink},
addressing the concerns related to the [expulsion of Cham
Albanians](expulsion_of_Cham_Albanians "expulsion of Cham Albanians"){.wikilink},
pursuing Euro-Atlantic integration and protecting the rights of the
Albanians in [Kosovo](Albanians_in_Kosovo "Kosovo"){.wikilink},
[Greece](Albanians_in_greece "Greece"){.wikilink},
[Italy](Arbëreshë_people "Italy"){.wikilink},
[Montenegro](Albanians_in_Montenegro "Montenegro"){.wikilink}, [North
Macedonia](Albanians_in_Macedonia "North Macedonia"){.wikilink},
[Serbia](Albanians_in_south_Serbia "Serbia"){.wikilink} and the
[diaspora](Albanian_diaspora "diaspora"){.wikilink}.[^213]

The external affairs of Albania underscore the country\'s dedication to
regional stability and integration into major international
institutions.[^214] Albania became a member of the [United
Nations](United_Nations "United Nations"){.wikilink} (UN) in 1955,
shortly after emerging from a period of isolation during the communist
era.[^215] The country reached a major achievement in its foreign policy
by securing NATO membership in 2009.[^216][^217] Since obtaining
candidate status in 2014, the country has also embarked on a
comprehensive reform agenda to align itself with European Union (EU)
accession standards, with the objective of becoming an EU member
state.[^218]

Albania and Kosovo maintain a fraternal relationship strengthened by
their substantial cultural, ethnical and historical ties.[^219] Both
countries foster enduring diplomatic ties, with Albania actively
supporting Kosovo\'s development and international integration
efforts.[^220] Its fundamental contribution to [Kosovo\'s path to
independence](2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence "Kosovo's path to independence"){.wikilink}
is underscored by its early [recognition of Kosovo\'s
sovereignty](International_recognition_of_Kosovo "recognition of Kosovo's sovereignty"){.wikilink}
in 2008.[^221] Furthermore, both governments hold annual joint meetings,
displayed by the inaugural meeting in 2014, which serves as an official
platform to enhance bilateral cooperation and reinforce their joint
commitment to policies that promote the stability and prosperity of the
broader Albanian region.[^222]

### Military

```{=mediawiki}
{{Main|Armed Forces of Albania}}
```
![[Albanian
soldiers](Albanian_Land_Force "Albanian soldiers"){.wikilink} in the
[Province of
Kandahar](Kandahar_Province "Province of Kandahar"){.wikilink},
Afghanistan](Albanian_special_operations_forces,_provide_security_as_Afghan_Border_Police_(ABP)_break_ground_on_a_new_checkpoint_in_the_district_of_Spin_Boldak,_Kandahar_province,_Afghanistan,_March_25,_2013_130325-A-MX357-127.jpg "Albanian soldiers in the Province of Kandahar, Afghanistan")

The [Albanian Armed
Forces](Albanian_Armed_Forces "Albanian Armed Forces"){.wikilink}
consist of [Land](Albanian_Land_Force "Land"){.wikilink},
[Air](Albanian_Air_Force "Air"){.wikilink} and [Naval
Forces](Albanian_Naval_Force "Naval Force"){.wikilink} and constitute
the military and paramilitary forces of the country. They are led by a
[commander-in-chief](commander-in-chief "commander-in-chief"){.wikilink}
under the supervision of the [Ministry of
Defence](Ministry_of_Defence_(Albania) "Ministry of Defence"){.wikilink}
and by the [President](President_of_Albania "President"){.wikilink} as
the supreme commander during wartime. However, in times of peace its
powers are executed through the [Prime
Minister](Prime_Minister_of_Albania "Prime Minister"){.wikilink} and the
[Defence
Minister](Ministry_of_Defence_(Albania) "Defence Minister"){.wikilink}.[^223]

The chief purpose of the armed forces of Albania is the defence of the
independence, the [sovereignty](sovereignty "sovereignty"){.wikilink}
and the [territorial
integrity](territorial_integrity "territorial integrity"){.wikilink} of
the country, as well as the participation in humanitarian, combat,
non-combat and peace support operations.[^224] [Military
service](Military_service "Military service"){.wikilink} is voluntary
since 2010 with the age of 19 being the legal minimum age for the
duty.[^225][^226]

Albania has committed to increase the participations in multinational
operations.[^227] Since the fall of communism, the country has
participated in six international missions but only one United Nations
mission in [Georgia](UNOMIG "Georgia"){.wikilink}, where it sent three
military observers. Since February 2008, Albania has participated
officially in NATO\'s [Operation Active
Endeavor](Operation_Active_Endeavor "Operation Active Endeavor"){.wikilink}
in the [Mediterranean
Sea](Mediterranean_Sea "Mediterranean Sea"){.wikilink}.[^228] It was
invited to join NATO on 3 April 2008, and it became a full member on 2
April 2009.[^229]

Albania reduced the number of active troops from 65,000 in 1988 to
14,500 in 2009.[^230][^231] The military now consists mainly of a small
fleet of aircraft and sea vessels. Increasing the military budget was
one of the most important conditions for [NATO](NATO "NATO"){.wikilink}
integration. As of 1996 military spending was an estimated 1.5% of the
country\'s GDP, only to peak in 2009 at 2% and fall again to 1.5%.[^232]

## Administrative divisions {#administrative_divisions}

```{=mediawiki}
{{Main|Administrative divisions of Albania}}
```
```{=mediawiki}
{{See also|Counties of Albania|Regions of Albania|Municipalities of Albania|Communes of Albania|Villages of Albania}}
```
```{=mediawiki}
{{image frame |content={{Albania Labelled Map}} |caption=The [[counties of Albania]] are the first-level administrative units in Albania.}}
```
Albania is defined within a territorial area of
`{{convert|28748|km2|0|abbr=on}}`{=mediawiki} in the [Balkan
Peninsula](Balkan_Peninsula "Balkan Peninsula"){.wikilink}. It is
informally divided into three regions, the
[Northern](Northern_Albania "Northern"){.wikilink},
[Central](Central_Albania "Central"){.wikilink} and [Southern
Regions](Southern_Albania "Southern Region"){.wikilink}. Since [its
Declaration of
Independence](Albanian_Declaration_of_Independence "its Declaration of Independence"){.wikilink}
in 1912, Albania has reformed [its internal
organisation](Administrative_divisions_of_Albania#History "its internal organisation"){.wikilink}
21 times. Presently, the primary [administrative
units](administrative_divisions_of_Albania "administrative units"){.wikilink}
are the twelve constituent
[counties](counties_of_Albania "counties"){.wikilink}
(`{{lang|sq|{{linktext|qarqe|lang=sq}}/{{linktext|qarqet|lang=sq}}}}`{=mediawiki}),
which hold equal status under the law.[^233] Counties had previously
been used in the 1950s and were recreated on 31 July 2000 to unify the
36 [districts](Districts_of_Albania "districts"){.wikilink}
(`{{lang|sq|{{linktext|rrathë|lang=sq}}/{{linktext|rrathët|lang=sq}}}}`{=mediawiki})
of that time.[^234][^235] The largest county in Albania by population is
[Tirana County](Tirana_County "Tirana County"){.wikilink} with over
800,000 people. The smallest county, by population, is [Gjirokastër
County](Gjirokastër_County "Gjirokastër County"){.wikilink} with over
70,000 people. The largest county, by area, is [Korçë
County](Korçë_County "Korçë County"){.wikilink} encompassing
`{{convert|3711|km²|sqmi}}`{=mediawiki} of the southeast of Albania. The
smallest county, by area, is [Durrës
County](Durrës_County "Durrës County"){.wikilink} with an area of
`{{convert|766|km²|sqmi}}`{=mediawiki} in the west of Albania.

The counties are made up of 61 second-level divisions known as
[municipalities](municipalities_of_Albania "municipalities"){.wikilink}
(`{{lang|sq|{{linktext|bashki|lang=sq}}/{{linktext|bashkia|lang=sq}}}}`{=mediawiki}).[^236]
The municipalities are the first level of local governance, responsible
for local needs and [law
enforcement](Law_enforcement_in_Albania "law enforcement"){.wikilink}.[^237][^238][^239]
They unified and simplified the previous system of
[urban](urban_municipalities_of_Albania "urban"){.wikilink} and [rural
municipalities](rural_municipalities_of_Albania "rural municipalities"){.wikilink}
or [communes](Communes_of_Albania "communes"){.wikilink}
(`{{lang|sq|{{linktext|komuna|lang=sq}}/{{linktext|komunat|lang=sq}}}}`{=mediawiki})
in 2015.[^240][^241] For smaller issues of [local
government](local_government "local government"){.wikilink}, the
municipalities are organised into 373 [administrative
units](administrative_units_of_Albania "administrative units"){.wikilink}
(`{{lang|sq|njësia}}`{=mediawiki}/`{{lang|sq|njësitë administrative}}`{=mediawiki}).
There are also 2980 villages
(`{{lang|sq|{{linktext|fshatra|lang=sq}}/{{linktext|fshatrat|lang=sq}}}}`{=mediawiki}),
neighborhoods or wards
(`{{lang|sq|{{linktext|lagje|lang=sq}}/{{linktext|lagjet|lang=sq}}}}`{=mediawiki}),
and localities
(`{{lang|sq|{{linktext|lokalitete|lang=sq}}/{{linktext|lokalitetet|lang=sq}}}}`{=mediawiki})
previously used as administrative units.

## Economy

```{=mediawiki}
{{Main|Economy of Albania}}
```
```{=mediawiki}
{{update section|date=May 2023}}
```
![[Tirana](Tirana "Tirana"){.wikilink} is the economic hub of the
country. It is home to major domestic and foreign companies operating in
the
country.](Toptani_Shopping_Mall_Tirana_2016.jpg "Tirana is the economic hub of the country. It is home to major domestic and foreign companies operating in the country.")

Albania\'s transition from a socialist [planned
economy](planned_economy "planned economy"){.wikilink} to a capitalist
[mixed economy](mixed_economy "mixed economy"){.wikilink} has been
largely successful.[^246] The country has a
[developing](Developing_country "developing"){.wikilink} mixed economy
classified by the [World Bank](World_Bank "World Bank"){.wikilink} as an
[upper-middle income
economy](List_of_countries_by_GNI_(nominal,_Atlas_method)_per_capita#Upper-middle-income_group "upper-middle income economy"){.wikilink}.
In 2016, it had the fourth-lowest [unemployment
rate](List_of_countries_by_unemployment_rate "unemployment rate"){.wikilink}
in the [Balkans](Balkans "Balkans"){.wikilink} with an estimated value
of 14.7%. Its largest trading partners are Italy, Greece, China, Spain,
Kosovo and the United States. The [lek](Albanian_lek "lek"){.wikilink}
(ALL) is the country\'s currency and is
[pegged](Fixed_exchange_rate "pegged"){.wikilink} at approximately
132.51 lek per euro.

The cities of [Tirana](Tirana "Tirana"){.wikilink} and
[Durrës](Durrës "Durrës"){.wikilink} constitute the economic and
financial heart of Albania due to their high population, modern
infrastructure and strategic geographical location. The country\'s most
important infrastructure facilities take course through both of the
cities, connecting the north to the south as well as the west to the
east. Among the largest
[companies](List_of_companies_of_Albania "companies"){.wikilink} are the
energy distribution public company
[OSHEE](Operatori_i_Shpërndarjes_së_Energjisë_Elektrike "OSHEE"){.wikilink},
steel producer Kurum, oil cdompanies like Kastrati,
[Albpetrol](Albpetrol "Albpetrol"){.wikilink}, and
[ARMO](ARMO_oil_refiner "ARMO"){.wikilink}, the mineral
[AlbChrome](AlbChrome "AlbChrome"){.wikilink}, the investment [BALFIN
Group](Samir_Mane "BALFIN Group"){.wikilink} and the telecommunications
companies [One Albania](Albtelecom "One Albania"){.wikilink} and
[Vodafone](Vodafone_Albania "Vodafone"){.wikilink}.[^247]

In 2012, Albania\'s [GDP per
capita](GDP_per_capita "GDP per capita"){.wikilink} stood at 30% of the
[European Union](European_Union "European Union"){.wikilink} average,
while [GDP (PPP) per
capita](GDP_(PPP)_per_capita "GDP (PPP) per capita"){.wikilink} was
35%.[^248] In the first quarter of 2010, after the [Great
Recession](Great_Recession "Great Recession"){.wikilink}, Albania was
one of three countries in Europe to record economic growth.[^249][^250]
The [International Monetary
Fund](International_Monetary_Fund "International Monetary Fund"){.wikilink}
predicted 2.6% growth for Albania in 2010 and 3.2% in 2011.[^251]
According to *[Forbes](Forbes "Forbes"){.wikilink}*,
`{{as of|2016|December|lc=y}}`{=mediawiki}, the [Gross Domestic Product
(GDP)](Gross_Domestic_Product_(GDP) "Gross Domestic Product (GDP)"){.wikilink}
was growing at 2.8%. The country had a [trade
balance](trade_balance "trade balance"){.wikilink} of −9.7% and
[unemployment rate](unemployment_rate "unemployment rate"){.wikilink} of
14.7%.[^252] [Foreign direct
investment](Foreign_direct_investment "Foreign direct investment"){.wikilink}
has increased significantly in recent years as the government has
embarked on an ambitious programme to improve the business climate
through fiscal and legislative reforms.

### Primary sector {#primary_sector}

```{=mediawiki}
{{main|Agriculture in Albania}}
```
![Grapes in [Berat](Berat "Berat"){.wikilink}. Due to the [Mediterranean
climate](Mediterranean_climate "Mediterranean climate"){.wikilink},
[wine](Albanian_wine "wine"){.wikilink},
[olives](olive "olive"){.wikilink} and [citrus
fruits](citrus_fruit "citrus fruit"){.wikilink} are mostly produced in
Southern
Albania.](Berat_kale_-_panoramio.jpg "Grapes in Berat. Due to the Mediterranean climate, wine, olives and citrus fruits are mostly produced in Southern Albania.")

Agriculture in the country is based on small to medium-sized
family-owned dispersed units. It remains a significant sector of the
[economy of
Albania](economy_of_Albania "economy of Albania"){.wikilink}. It employs
41%[^253] of the population, and about 24.31% of the land is used for
agricultural purposes. One of the earliest farming sites in Europe has
been found in the southeast of the country.[^254] As part of the
pre-accession process of Albania to the [European
Union](European_Union "European Union"){.wikilink}, farmers are being
aided through
[IPA](Instrument_for_Pre-Accession_Assistance "IPA"){.wikilink} funds to
improve Albanian agriculture standards.[^255]

Albania produces significant amounts of fruits (apples,
[olives](olive "olive"){.wikilink}, grapes, oranges, lemons,
[apricots](apricot "apricot"){.wikilink},
[peaches](peach "peach"){.wikilink},
[cherries](Cherry "cherries"){.wikilink},
[figs](figs "figs"){.wikilink}, [sour
cherries](Prunus_cerasus "sour cherries"){.wikilink},
[plums](plum "plum"){.wikilink}, and
[strawberries](Strawberry "strawberries"){.wikilink}),
[vegetables](Vegetable_oil "vegetables"){.wikilink} (potatoes, tomatoes,
[maize](maize "maize"){.wikilink}, onions, and wheat), [sugar
beets](sugar_beet "sugar beet"){.wikilink}, tobacco, meat,
[honey](honey "honey"){.wikilink}, [dairy
products](dairy_product "dairy product"){.wikilink}, traditional
medicine and [aromatic
plants](Essential_oil "aromatic plants"){.wikilink}. Further, the
country is a worldwide significant producer of
[salvia](salvia "salvia"){.wikilink},
[rosemary](rosemary "rosemary"){.wikilink} and [yellow
gentian](Gentiana_lutea "yellow gentian"){.wikilink}.[^256] The
country\'s proximity to the [Ionian
Sea](Ionian_Sea "Ionian Sea"){.wikilink} and the [Adriatic
Sea](Adriatic_Sea "Adriatic Sea"){.wikilink} give the underdeveloped
fishing industry great potential. The [World
Bank](World_Bank "World Bank"){.wikilink} and [European
Community](European_Community "European Community"){.wikilink}
economists report that, Albania\'s fishing industry has good potential
to generate export earnings because prices in the nearby Greek and
Italian markets are many times higher than those in the Albanian market.
The fish available off the coasts of the country are
[carp](carp "carp"){.wikilink}, [trout](trout "trout"){.wikilink}, [sea
bream](sea_bream "sea bream"){.wikilink},
[mussels](mussel "mussel"){.wikilink} and
[crustaceans](crustacean "crustacean"){.wikilink}.

Albania has one of Europe\'s longest histories of
[viticulture](viticulture "viticulture"){.wikilink}.[^257] Today\'s
region was one of the few places where vine was naturally grown during
the ice age. The oldest found seeds in the region are 4,000 to 6,000
years old.[^258] In 2009, the nation produced an estimated 17,500 tonnes
of wine.[^259]

### Secondary sector {#secondary_sector}

```{=mediawiki}
{{See also|Category:Mines in Albania}}
```
![The [Antea](Antea_Cement "Antea"){.wikilink} factory in
[Fushë-Krujë](Fushë-Krujë "Fushë-Krujë"){.wikilink}](Something_in_Albania_(10759257413).jpg "The Antea factory in Fushë-Krujë")

Albania\'s secondary sector has undergone many changes and
diversification since the communist regime collapsed. It is very
diversified, from
[electronics](Electronics_industry "electronics"){.wikilink},
[manufacturing](Manufacturing_industries "manufacturing"){.wikilink},[^260]
[textiles](Textile_industry "textiles"){.wikilink}, to
[food](Food_industry "food"){.wikilink},
[cement](Cement_industry "cement"){.wikilink},
[mining](Mining_industry "mining"){.wikilink},[^261] and
[energy](Energy_industry "energy"){.wikilink}. The [Antea
Cement](Antea_Cement "Antea Cement"){.wikilink} plant in
[Fushë-Krujë](Fushë-Krujë "Fushë-Krujë"){.wikilink} is considered one of
the nation\'s largest industrial greenfield investments.[^262] Albanian
oil and gas is one of the most promising, albeit strictly regulated,
sectors of its economy. Albania has the [second-largest oil
deposits](List_of_countries_by_proven_oil_reserves "second-largest oil deposits"){.wikilink}
in the [Balkan
peninsula](Balkan_peninsula "Balkan peninsula"){.wikilink} after
[Romania](Romania "Romania"){.wikilink}, and the largest [oil
reserves](Patos-Marinza_Oil_Field "oil reserves"){.wikilink}[^263] in
Europe. The [Albpetrol](Albpetrol "Albpetrol"){.wikilink} company is
owned by the Albanian state and monitors the state petroleum agreements
in the country. The textile industry has seen an extensive expansion by
approaching companies from the [European
Union](European_Union "European Union"){.wikilink} (EU) in Albania.
According to the [Instituti i Statistikës
(INSTAT)](Institute_of_Statistics_(Albania) "Instituti i Statistikës (INSTAT)"){.wikilink},
`{{As of|2016|lc=y}}`{=mediawiki}, textile production had an annual
growth of 5.3% and an annual turnover of around 1.5 billion euros.[^264]

Albania is a significant minerals producer and ranks among the world\'s
leading [chromium](chromium "chromium"){.wikilink} producers and
exporters.[^265] The nation is also a notable producer of copper,
nickel, and coal.[^266] The [Batra
mine](Batra_mine "Batra mine"){.wikilink}, [Bulqizë
mine](Bulqizë_mine "Bulqizë mine"){.wikilink}, and [Thekna
mine](Thekna_mine "Thekna mine"){.wikilink} are among the most
recognised Albanian mines still in operation.

### Tertiary sector {#tertiary_sector}

```{=mediawiki}
{{see also|Banking in Albania|Telecommunications in Albania|Tourism in Albania|l1=Banking|l2=Telecommunications}}
```
![The [Islets of
Ksamil](Islets_of_Ksamil "Islets of Ksamil"){.wikilink}, in the south of
the [Albanian Ionian Sea
Coast](Albanian_Ionian_Sea_Coast "Albanian Ionian Sea Coast"){.wikilink}](Ksamil_Albania_._Albanian_Riviera.jpg "The Islets of Ksamil, in the south of the Albanian Ionian Sea Coast")
The [tertiary sector](tertiary_sector "tertiary sector"){.wikilink}
represents the fastest growing sector of the country\'s economy. 36% of
the population work in the service sector which contributes to 65% of
the country\'s GDP.[^267] Ever since the end of the 20th century, the
[banking industry](banking_industry "banking industry"){.wikilink} is a
major component of the tertiary sector and remains in good conditions
overall due to [privatisation](privatisation "privatisation"){.wikilink}
and the commendable [monetary
policy](monetary_policy "monetary policy"){.wikilink}.[^268][^269]

Previously one of the most
[isolated](Isolationism "isolated"){.wikilink} and controlled countries
in the world, [telecommunication
industry](telecommunication_industry "telecommunication industry"){.wikilink}
represents nowadays another major contributor to the sector. It
developed largely through privatisation and subsequent investment by
both domestic and foreign investors.[^270]
[Eagle](Eagle_Mobile "Eagle"){.wikilink},
[Vodafone](Vodafone_Albania "Vodafone"){.wikilink} and [Telekom
Albania](Telekom_Albania "Telekom Albania"){.wikilink} are the leading
[telecommunications service
providers](telecommunications_service_provider "telecommunications service provider"){.wikilink}
in the country.

Tourism is recognised as an industry of national importance and has been
steadily increasing since the beginnings of the 21st
century.[^271][^272] It directly accounted for 8.4% of GDP in 2016
though including indirect contributions pushes the proportion to
26%.[^273] In the same year, the country received approximately
4.74 million visitors mostly from across Europe and the United States as
well.[^274]

The increase of foreign visitors has been dramatic. Albania had only
500,000 visitors in 2005, and an estimated 4.2 million in 2012, an
increase of 740 percent. In 2015, summer tourism increased by 25 percent
from 2014, according to the country\'s tourism agency.[^275] In 2011,
[Lonely Planet](Lonely_Planet "Lonely Planet"){.wikilink} named Albania
as a top travel
destination,[^276]`{{failed verification|date=November 2017|reason=How could a 2011 article talk about 2015? anyway link needs updating}}`{=mediawiki}
while *[The New York
Times](The_New_York_Times "The New York Times"){.wikilink}* placed
Albania as number 4 global tourist destination in 2014.[^277]

The bulk of the tourist industry is concentrated along the
[Adriatic](Adriatic "Adriatic"){.wikilink} and [Ionian
Sea](Ionian_Sea "Ionian Sea"){.wikilink} in the west of the country. But
the [Albanian Riviera](Albanian_Riviera "Albanian Riviera"){.wikilink}
in the southwest has the most scenic and pristine beaches; its coastline
has a considerable length of
`{{convert|446|km|abbr=off}}`{=mediawiki}.[^278] The coast has a
distinctive character, rich in varieties of virgin beaches, capes,
coves, covered bays, lagoons, small gravel beaches, sea caves, and many
landforms. Some parts of this seaside are very clean ecologically,
including unexplored areas, which are very rare within the
[Mediterranean](Mediterranean "Mediterranean"){.wikilink}.[^279] Other
attractions include the mountainous areas such as the [Albanian
Alps](Albanian_Alps "Albanian Alps"){.wikilink}, [Ceraunian
Mountains](Ceraunian_Mountains "Ceraunian Mountains"){.wikilink} and
[Korab](Korab "Korab"){.wikilink} Mountains but also the historical
cities of [Berat](Berat "Berat"){.wikilink},
[Durrës](Durrës "Durrës"){.wikilink},
[Gjirokastër](Gjirokastër "Gjirokastër"){.wikilink},
[Sarandë](Sarandë "Sarandë"){.wikilink},
[Shkodër](Shkodër "Shkodër"){.wikilink} and
[Korçë](Korçë "Korçë"){.wikilink}.

### Transport

```{=mediawiki}
{{Main|Transport in Albania}}
```
![[Rruga e Kombit](Durrës-Kukës_Highway "Rruga e Kombit"){.wikilink}
connects the [Adriatic Sea](Adriatic_Sea "Adriatic Sea"){.wikilink}
across the [Western
Lowlands](Western_Lowlands "Western Lowlands"){.wikilink} with the
[Albanian
Alps](Albanian_Alps "Albanian Alps"){.wikilink}.](Autostrada_Durrës-Morina-05.jpg "Rruga e Kombit connects the Adriatic Sea across the Western Lowlands with the Albanian Alps.")

Transportation in Albania is managed within the functions of the
[Ministry of Infrastructure and
Energy](Ministry_of_Infrastructure_and_Energy_(Albania) "Ministry of Infrastructure and Energy"){.wikilink}
and entities such as the [Albanian Road
Authority](Albanian_Road_Authority "Albanian Road Authority"){.wikilink}
(ARRSH), responsible for the construction and maintenance of the
[highways](Highways_in_Albania "highways"){.wikilink} and
[motorways](motorways_in_Albania "motorways"){.wikilink} in Albania, as
well as the [Albanian Aviation
Authority](Civil_Aviation_Authority_(Albania) "Albanian Aviation Authority"){.wikilink}
(AAC), with the responsibility of coordinating civil aviation and
airports in the country.

The [international
airport](Tirana_International_Airport_Nënë_Tereza "international airport"){.wikilink}
of [Tirana](Tirana "Tirana"){.wikilink} is the premier air gateway to
the country, and is also the principal hub for Albania\'s national [flag
carrier](flag_carrier "flag carrier"){.wikilink} airline, [Air
Albania](Air_Albania "Air Albania"){.wikilink}. The airport carried more
than 3.3 million passengers in 2019 with connections to many
destinations in other countries around
[Europe](Europe "Europe"){.wikilink},
[Africa](Africa "Africa"){.wikilink} and
[Asia](Asia "Asia"){.wikilink}.[^280] The country plans to progressively
increase the number of airports especially in the south with possible
locations in [Sarandë](Sarandë "Sarandë"){.wikilink},
[Gjirokastër](Gjirokastër "Gjirokastër"){.wikilink} and
[Vlorë](Vlorë_International_Airport "Vlorë"){.wikilink}.[^281]

The [highways](Highways_in_Albania "highways"){.wikilink} and [motorways
in Albania](motorways_in_Albania "motorways in Albania"){.wikilink} are
properly maintained and often still under construction and renovation.
The [Autostrada 1](A1_motorway_(Albania) "Autostrada 1"){.wikilink} (A1)
is an integral transportation corridor and the country\'s longest
motorway. It is planned to link [Durrës](Durrës "Durrës"){.wikilink} on
the Adriatic Sea across [Pristina](Pristina "Pristina"){.wikilink} in
Kosovo with the [Pan-European Corridor
X](Pan-European_Corridor_X "Pan-European Corridor X"){.wikilink} in
Serbia.[^282][^283] The [Autostrada
2](A2_motorway_(Albania) "Autostrada 2"){.wikilink} (A2) is part of the
[Adriatic--Ionian
Corridor](Adriatic–Ionian_motorway "Adriatic–Ionian Corridor"){.wikilink}
as well as the [Pan-European Corridor
VIII](Pan-European_Corridor_VIII "Pan-European Corridor VIII"){.wikilink}
and connects [Fier](Fier "Fier"){.wikilink} with
[Vlorë](Vlorë "Vlorë"){.wikilink}.[^284] The [Autostrada
3](A3_motorway_(Albania) "Autostrada 3"){.wikilink} (A3) is under
construction and after its completion will connect
[Tirana](Tirana "Tirana"){.wikilink} and
[Elbasan](Elbasan "Elbasan"){.wikilink} with the Pan-European Corridor
VIII. When all three corridors are completed, Albania will have an
estimated `{{convert|759|km}}`{=mediawiki} of highway, linking it with
all neighboring countries.

[Durrës](Port_of_Durrës "Durrës"){.wikilink} is the busiest and largest
[seaport](seaport "seaport"){.wikilink} in the country, followed by
[Vlorë](Port_of_Vlorë "Vlorë"){.wikilink},
[Shëngjin](Port_of_Shëngjin "Shëngjin"){.wikilink} and
[Sarandë](Port_of_Sarandë "Sarandë"){.wikilink}.
`{{as of|2014}}`{=mediawiki}, it is as one of the largest passenger
ports on the [Adriatic Sea](Adriatic_Sea "Adriatic Sea"){.wikilink},
with annual passenger volume of about 1.5 million. The principal ports
serve a system of ferries connecting Albania with islands and coastal
cities in Croatia, Greece, and Italy.

The rail network is administered by the national railway company
[Hekurudha
Shqiptare](Hekurudha_Shqiptare "Hekurudha Shqiptare"){.wikilink}, which
was extensively promoted by Hoxha. There has been considerable increase
in private car ownership and bus usage while rail use decreased since
the end of communism. A new railway line from Tirana and its airport to
Durrës is planned. The location of this railway, connecting Albania\'s
most populated urban areas, makes it an important economic development
project.[^285][^286]

## Infrastructure

### Education

```{=mediawiki}
{{Main|Education in Albania}}
```
![The [University of
Arts](University_of_Arts_(Albania) "University of Arts"){.wikilink} is
the largest higher education institute dedicated to the study of
arts](Akademia_e_arteve_Ergys_Veliu_Photography.jpg "The University of Arts is the largest higher education institute dedicated to the study of arts")

In Albania, education is secular, free,
[compulsory](Compulsory_education "compulsory"){.wikilink}, and based on
three levels.[^287][^288] The academic year is apportioned into two
semesters, beginning in September or October and ending in June or July.
[Albanian](Albanian_language "Albanian"){.wikilink} is the [primary
language](primary_language "primary language"){.wikilink} of instruction
in the country\'s [academic
institutions](state_school "academic institution"){.wikilink}.[^289] The
study of a first [foreign
language](foreign_language "foreign language"){.wikilink} is mandatory
and taught most often at elementary and bilingual schools.[^290]
Languages taught in schools are English, Italian, French and
German.[^291] Albania has a [school life
expectancy](school_life_expectancy "school life expectancy"){.wikilink}
of 16 years and a [literacy
rate](literacy_rate "literacy rate"){.wikilink} of 98.7%, with 99.2% for
men and 98.3% for women.[^292][^293]

Compulsory primary education is divided into two levels, elementary and
secondary school, from grade one to five and six to nine,
respectively.[^294] Pupils are required to attend school from the age
six until they turn 16. Upon successful completion of primary education,
all pupils are entitled to attend high schools, specialising in any
field, including arts, sports, languages, sciences, and
technology.[^295]

Tertiary education is optional and has undergone a thorough reformation
and restructuring in compliance with the principles of the [Bologna
Process](Bologna_Process "Bologna Process"){.wikilink}. There are a
significant number of private and public [institutions of higher
education](institutions_of_higher_education "institutions of higher education"){.wikilink}
in Albania\'s major cities.[^296][^297] Tertiary education is organised
into three successive levels, the
[bachelor](Bachelor's_degree "bachelor"){.wikilink},
[master](Master's_degree "master"){.wikilink}, and
[doctorate](Doctorate_Degree "doctorate"){.wikilink}.

### Health

```{=mediawiki}
{{Main|Health in Albania}}
```
![The [Albanian cuisine](Albanian_cuisine "Albanian cuisine"){.wikilink}
from the Mediterranean, which is characterised by the use of fruits,
vegetables and [olive oil](olive_oil "olive oil"){.wikilink},
contributes to the good nutrition of the country\'s
population[^298]](Olive-oil-1412361_1920.jpg "The Albanian cuisine from the Mediterranean, which is characterised by the use of fruits, vegetables and olive oil, contributes to the good nutrition of the country's population")

The [constitution of
Albania](constitution_of_Albania "constitution of Albania"){.wikilink}
guarantees its citizens equal, free, and [universal health
care](universal_health_care "universal health care"){.wikilink}.[^300]
The health care system is organised into
[primary](Primary_healthcare "primary"){.wikilink},
[secondary](Secondary_care "secondary"){.wikilink}, and [tertiary
healthcare](tertiary_healthcare "tertiary healthcare"){.wikilink}, and
is in a process of modernisation and development.[^301][^302] The [life
expectancy](life_expectancy "life expectancy"){.wikilink} at birth in
Albania is 77.8 years, ranking
[37th](List_of_countries_by_life_expectancy "37th"){.wikilink} in the
world and surpassing several [developed
countries](developed_countries "developed countries"){.wikilink}.[^303]
The average [healthy life
expectancy](Life_expectancy#Healthy_life_expectancy "healthy life expectancy"){.wikilink}
is 68.8 years, ranking 37th in the world.[^304] The country\'s [infant
mortality
rate](infant_mortality_rate "infant mortality rate"){.wikilink} was
estimated at 12 per 1,000 live births in 2015. In 2000, the country had
the world\'s 55th-best healthcare performance, as defined by the [World
Health
Organisation](World_Health_Organization "World Health Organisation"){.wikilink}
(WHO).[^305]

[Cardiovascular
disease](Cardiovascular_disease "Cardiovascular disease"){.wikilink} is
the principal cause of death in Albania, accounting for 52% of
deaths.[^306] [Accidents](Accident "Accident"){.wikilink}, injuries,
[malignant](Malignant_disease "malignant"){.wikilink} and [respiratory
diseases](respiratory_disease "respiratory disease"){.wikilink} are
other primary causes of death.[^307] [Neuropsychiatric
disease](Neuropsychiatric_disorders "Neuropsychiatric disease"){.wikilink}
has also increased due to recent demographic, social, and economic
changes in the country.[^308]

In 2009, Albania had a fruit and vegetable supply of 886 grams per
capita per day, the fifth-highest supply in Europe.[^309] Compared to
other developed and developing countries, Albania has a relatively low
rate of [obesity](obesity "obesity"){.wikilink}, probably thanks to the
[Mediterranean
diet](Mediterranean_diet "Mediterranean diet"){.wikilink}.[^310][^311]
According to [2016 WHO
data](List_of_countries_by_Body_Mass_Index_(BMI)#WHO_Data_on_Prevalence_of_Obesity_(BMI_above_30)_(2014) "2016 WHO data"){.wikilink},
21.7% of adults in the country are clinically
[overweight](overweight "overweight"){.wikilink}, with a [Body mass
index](Body_mass_index "Body mass index"){.wikilink} (BMI) score of 25
or more.[^312]

### Energy

```{=mediawiki}
{{Main|Renewable energy in Albania}}
```
```{=mediawiki}
{{See also|List of power stations in Albania|List of oil and gas fields in Albania|l1=Power stations|l2=Oil fields in Albania}}
```
![Electricity production in Albania from 1980 to
2019](Albania_electricity_production.svg "Electricity production in Albania from 1980 to 2019")

Due to its location and natural resources, Albania has a wide variety of
[energy resources](energy_resource "energy resource"){.wikilink},
ranging from gas, oil, and coal to
[wind](Wind_energy "wind"){.wikilink},
[solar](Solar_energy "solar"){.wikilink},
[water](hydropower "water"){.wikilink}, and other
[renewable](renewable_energy "renewable"){.wikilink}
sources.[^313][^314] According to the [World Economic
Forum](World_Economic_Forum "World Economic Forum"){.wikilink}\'s 2023
Energy Transition Index (ETI), the country ranked 21st globally,
highlighting the progress in its energy transition agenda.[^315]
Currently, Albania\'s electricity generation sector depends on
[hydroelectricity](hydroelectricity "hydroelectricity"){.wikilink},
ranking fifth in the world in percentage terms.[^316][^317][^318]
Increasing risks of river floods and droughts due to [climate
change](climate_change "climate change"){.wikilink} is expected to put
electricity generation at risk.[^319] The
[Drin](Drin_(river) "Drin"){.wikilink}, in the north, hosts four
[hydroelectric power
stations](hydroelectric_power_station "hydroelectric power station"){.wikilink},
including
[Fierza](Fierza_Hydroelectric_Power_Station "Fierza"){.wikilink},
[Koman](Koman_Hydroelectric_Power_Station "Koman"){.wikilink},
[Skavica](Skavica_Hydro_Power_Plant "Skavica"){.wikilink} and [Vau i
Dejës](Vau_i_Dejës_Hydroelectric_Power_Station "Vau i Dejës"){.wikilink}.
Two other power stations, such as the
[Banjë](Banjë_Hydro_Power_Plant "Banjë"){.wikilink} and
[Moglicë](Moglicë_Hydro_Power_Plant "Moglicë"){.wikilink}, are along the
[Devoll](Devoll_(river) "Devoll"){.wikilink} in the south.[^320]

Albania has considerable oil deposits. It has the 10th-largest oil
reserves in Europe and the 58th in the world.[^321] The country\'s main
petroleum deposits are located around the [Albanian Adriatic Sea
Coast](Albanian_Adriatic_Sea_Coast "Albanian Adriatic Sea Coast"){.wikilink}
and [Myzeqe](Myzeqe "Myzeqe"){.wikilink} Plain within the [Western
Lowlands](Western_Lowlands "Western Lowlands"){.wikilink}, where the
country\'s largest reserve is located.
[Patos-Marinza](Patos-Marinza_Oil_Field "Patos-Marinza"){.wikilink},
also located within the area, is the largest onshore [oil
field](oil_field "oil field"){.wikilink} in Europe.[^322] The [Trans
Adriatic
Pipeline](Trans_Adriatic_Pipeline "Trans Adriatic Pipeline"){.wikilink}
(TAP), part of the planned [Southern Gas
Corridor](Southern_Gas_Corridor "Southern Gas Corridor"){.wikilink},
runs for `{{convert|215|km|0|abbr=off}}`{=mediawiki} across Albania\'s
territory before entering the [Albanian Adriatic Sea
Coast](Albanian_Adriatic_Sea_Coast "Albanian Adriatic Sea Coast"){.wikilink}
approximately `{{convert|17|km|0|abbr=off}}`{=mediawiki} northwest of
[Fier](Fier "Fier"){.wikilink}.[^323]

Albania\'s [water
resources](water_resources "water resources"){.wikilink} are
particularly abundant in all the regions of the country and comprise
[lakes](Lakes_of_Albania "lakes"){.wikilink},
[rivers](Rivers_of_Albania "rivers"){.wikilink}, springs, and
groundwater aquifers.[^324] The country\'s available average quantity of
[fresh water](fresh_water "fresh water"){.wikilink} is estimated at
`{{convert|129.7|m3|0|abbr=off}}`{=mediawiki} per inhabitant per year,
one of the highest rates in Europe.[^325] According to data presented by
the [Joint Monitoring Programme for Water Supply and
Sanitation](Joint_Monitoring_Programme_for_Water_Supply_and_Sanitation "Joint Monitoring Programme for Water Supply and Sanitation"){.wikilink}
(JMP) in 2015, about 93% of the country\'s total population had access
to [improved
sanitation](improved_sanitation "improved sanitation"){.wikilink}.[^326]

### Media

```{=mediawiki}
{{Main|Media in Albania}}
```
```{=mediawiki}
{{See also|Cinema of Albania}}
```
![The former grounds of the headquarters of [Radio
Tirana](Radio_Tirana "Radio Tirana"){.wikilink} in the capital of
[Tirana](Tirana "Tirana"){.wikilink}.
`{{lang|sq|[[Radio Televizioni Shqiptar]]|italic=no}}`{=mediawiki}
(RTSH) was initially inaugurated as Radio Tirana in 1938 prior to the
[World War
II](World_War_II "World War II"){.wikilink}](Villa_of_the_former_Radio_Tirana_(03).jpg "The former grounds of the headquarters of Radio Tirana in the capital of Tirana.  (RTSH) was initially inaugurated as Radio Tirana in 1938 prior to the World War II")

The [freedom of press](freedom_of_press "freedom of press"){.wikilink}
and [speech](Freedom_of_speech "speech"){.wikilink}, and the right to
free expression is guaranteed in the [constitution of
Albania](constitution_of_Albania "constitution of Albania"){.wikilink}.[^327]
Albania was ranked 84th on the [Press Freedom
Index](Press_Freedom_Index "Press Freedom Index"){.wikilink} of 2020
compiled by the [Reporters Without
Borders](Reporters_Without_Borders "Reporters Without Borders"){.wikilink},
with its score steadily declining since 2003.[^328] Nevertheless, in the
2020 report of [Freedom in the
World](Freedom_in_the_World "Freedom in the World"){.wikilink}, the
[Freedom House](Freedom_House "Freedom House"){.wikilink} classified the
freedoms of press and speech in Albania as partly free from political
interference and manipulation.[^329]

```{=mediawiki}
{{lang|sq|[[Radio Televizioni Shqiptar]]|italic=no}}
```
(RTSH) is the [national
broadcaster](national_broadcaster "national broadcaster"){.wikilink}
corporation of Albania operating numerous television and radio stations
in the country.[^330] The three major private broadcaster corporations
are [Top Channel](Top_Channel "Top Channel"){.wikilink}, [Televizioni
Klan](TV_Klan "Televizioni Klan"){.wikilink} and [Vizion
Plus](Vizion_Plus "Vizion Plus"){.wikilink} whose content are
distributed throughout Albania and beyond its territory in
[Kosovo](Kosovo "Kosovo"){.wikilink} and other
[Albanian-speaking](Albanian_language "Albanian-speaking"){.wikilink}
territories.

Albanian cinema has its roots in the 20th century and developed after
the country\'s [declaration of
independence](Albanian_Declaration_of_Independence "declaration of independence"){.wikilink}.[^331]
The first [movie theater](movie_theater "movie theater"){.wikilink}
exclusively devoted to showing [motion
pictures](motion_pictures "motion pictures"){.wikilink} was built in
1912 in [Shkodër](Shkodër "Shkodër"){.wikilink}.[^332] During the
[People\'s Republic of
Albania](People's_Republic_of_Albania "People's Republic of Albania"){.wikilink},
Albanian cinema developed rapidly with the inauguration of the
[Kinostudio Shqipëria e
Re](Kinostudio_Shqipëria_e_Re "Kinostudio Shqipëria e Re"){.wikilink} in
Tirana.[^333] In 1953, the Albanian-Soviet [epic
film](epic_film "epic film"){.wikilink}, the [Great Warrior
Skanderbeg](The_Great_Warrior_Skanderbeg "Great Warrior Skanderbeg"){.wikilink},
was released chronicling the life and fight of the medieval Albanian
hero [Skanderbeg](Gjergj_Kastriot_Skanderbeg "Skanderbeg"){.wikilink}.
It went on to win the international prize at the [1954 Cannes Film
Festival](1954_Cannes_Film_Festival "1954 Cannes Film Festival"){.wikilink}.
In 2003, the [Tirana International Film
Festival](Tirana_International_Film_Festival "Tirana International Film Festival"){.wikilink}
was established, the largest film festival in the country. The [Durrës
Amphitheatre](Durrës_Amphitheatre "Durrës Amphitheatre"){.wikilink} is
host to the [Durrës International Film
Festival](Durrës_International_Film_Festival "Durrës International Film Festival"){.wikilink},
the second largest film festival.

### Technology

```{=mediawiki}
{{Main|Science and technology in Albania|Telecommunications in Albania|l1=Technology}}
```
After the [fall of
communism](Fall_of_communism_in_Albania "fall of communism"){.wikilink}
in 1991, human resources in sciences and technology in Albania have
drastically decreased. As of various reports, during 1991 to 2005
approximately 50% of the professors and scientists of the universities
and science institutions in the country have left Albania.[^334] In
2009, the [government](Government_of_Albania "government"){.wikilink}
approved the National Strategy for Science, Technology and Innovation in
Albania covering the period 2009 to 2015.[^335] It aims to triple public
spending on [research and
development](research_and_development "research and development"){.wikilink}
to 0.6% of GDP and augment the share of
[GDE](Gross_domestic_expenditure_on_R&D "GDE"){.wikilink} from foreign
sources, including the framework programmes for research of the
[European Union](European_Union "European Union"){.wikilink}, to the
point where it covers 40% of research spending, among others. Albania
was ranked 84th in the [Global Innovation
Index](Global_Innovation_Index "Global Innovation Index"){.wikilink} in
2024.[^336]

Telecommunication represents one of the fastest growing and dynamic
sectors in Albania.[^337][^338] [Vodafone
Albania](Vodafone_Albania "Vodafone Albania"){.wikilink}, [Telekom
Albania](Telekom_Albania "Telekom Albania"){.wikilink} and
[Albtelecom](Albtelecom "Albtelecom"){.wikilink} are the three large
providers of [mobile](Mobile_network_operator "mobile"){.wikilink} and
[internet](internet "internet"){.wikilink} in Albania.[^339] As of the
[Electronic and Postal Communications
Authority](Electronic_and_Postal_Communications_Authority_(Albania) "Electronic and Postal Communications Authority"){.wikilink}
(AKEP) in 2018, the country had approximately 2.7 million active mobile
users with almost 1.8 million active broadband subscribers.[^340]
Vodafone Albania alone served more than 931,000 mobile users, Telekom
Albania had about 605,000 users and Albtelecom had more than 272,000
users.[^341] In [January
2023](List_of_spaceflight_launches_in_January–June_2023 "January 2023"){.wikilink},
Albania launched its [first two
satellites](List_of_first_satellites_by_country "first two satellites"){.wikilink},
*Albania 1* and *Albania 2*, into [orbit](orbit "orbit"){.wikilink}, in
what was regarded as a milestone effort in monitoring the country\'s
territory and identifying illegal activities.[^342][^343]
Albanian-American engineer [Mira
Murati](Mira_Murati "Mira Murati"){.wikilink}, the Chief Technology
Officer of research organisation [OpenAI](OpenAI "OpenAI"){.wikilink},
played a substantial role in the development and launch of artificial
intelligence services such as [ChatGPT](ChatGPT "ChatGPT"){.wikilink},
[Codex](OpenAI_Codex "Codex"){.wikilink} and
[DALL-E](DALL-E "DALL-E"){.wikilink}.[^344][^345][^346] In December
2023, Prime Minister Edi Rama announced plans for collaboration between
the Albanian government and ChatGPT, facilitated by discussions with
Murati.[^347][^348] Rama emphasised the intention to streamline the
alignment of Albanian laws with the regulations of the European Union,
aiming to reduce costs associated with translation and legal
services.[^349]

## Demography

```{=mediawiki}
{{Main|Demographics of Albania|l1=Demography of Albania}}
```
```{=mediawiki}
{{See also|Albanian people|Origin of the Albanians}}
```
![Development of the [population of
Albania](Demographics_of_Albania "population of Albania"){.wikilink}
over the last sixty
years](Albania_demography.svg "Development of the population of Albania over the last sixty years")

The demographic statistics of Albania, as revealed by the 2023 census
conducted by the [Instituti i
Statistikave](Institute_of_Statistics_(Albania) "Instituti i Statistikave"){.wikilink}
(INSTAT), indicated a population of 2,402,113, with a notable decline
from the 2,821,977 recorded in the 2011
census.`{{sfn|2023 Albanian census|2024|p=105}}`{=mediawiki}`{{sfn|2011 Albanian census|2012|p=7}}`{=mediawiki}
The decrease in inhabitants began after the disintegration of the
communist regime in Albania and is associated with significant shifts
within the political, economic, and social structure of
Albania.`{{sfn|Population Dynamics|2014|p=25}}`{=mediawiki}`{{sfn|2023 Albanian census|2024|p=114}}`{=mediawiki}
A principal factor in this transition incorporates a decline in
fertility rates coupled with an increase in emigration, both
contributing to persistent demographic changes and
challenges.`{{sfn|Population Dynamics|2014|p=39}}`{=mediawiki} It is
forecast that the population will continue shrinking for the next decade
at least, depending on the actual rates and the level of
migration.[^350] Currently, the population density of Albania is
measured at 83.6 inhabitants per square kilometer with a varied
distribution of inhabitants across different
regions.`{{sfn|2023 Albanian census|2024|p=105}}`{=mediawiki}[^351] The
counties of [Tirana](Tirana_County "Tirana"){.wikilink} and
[Durrës](Durrës_County "Durrës"){.wikilink} showcase substantial
concentrations of people, accounting for about 41% of the overall
demographic of Albania, with 32% residing in Tirana and 9% in
Durrës.`{{sfn|2023 Albanian census|2024|p=117}}`{=mediawiki} Conversely,
more peripheral and rural counties such as
[Gjirokastër](Gjirokastër_County "Gjirokastër"){.wikilink} and
[Kukës](Kukës_County "Kukës"){.wikilink} present significantly lower
population densities, with each aiding 3% to the overall
population.`{{sfn|2023 Albanian census|2024|p=117}}`{=mediawiki}

Historically, the Albanian people have established several communities
in many regions throughout Southern Europe. The [Albanian
diaspora](Albanian_diaspora "Albanian diaspora"){.wikilink} has been
formed since the late Middle Ages, when they emigrated to escape either
various socio-political difficulties or the Ottoman conquest of
Albania.[^352] Following the fall of communism, large numbers of
Albanians have migrated to countries such as Australia, Canada,
Switzerland, the United Kingdom and the United States. Albanian
[minorities](Minority_group "minorities"){.wikilink} are present in the
neighbouring territories such as the west of North Macedonia, the
southeast of Montenegro, Kosovo in its entirety and parts of southern
Serbia. Altogether, the number of ethnic Albanians living abroad is
estimated to be higher than the total population inside Albania. As much
as a third of those born in the country\'s borders now live outside of
it, making Albania one of the countries with the highest rate of
outmigration relative to its population in the world.[^353][^354] In
2022 the birth rate was 20% lower than in 2021, largely due to
emigration of people of childbearing age.[^355]

### Urbanisation

```{=mediawiki}
{{Main|List of cities and towns in Albania}}
```
Subsequent to the collapse of communism in 1991, Albania has undergone a
remarkable transformation in its urban landscape, emerging as one of the
fastest urbanising countries in
Europe.`{{sfn|Internal Migration Albania|2014|p=12}}`{=mediawiki}[^356][^357]
At the forefront of this transformation is the
[Tirana](Tirana_County "Tirana"){.wikilink}-[Durrës](Durrës_County "Durrës"){.wikilink}
agglomeration, a densely populated urban corridor situated along the
[western coast of
Albania](Albanian_Coastal_Lowlands "western coast of Albania"){.wikilink}.[^358]
This corridor has become the primary locus of population growth and
settlement development, attracting a significant influx of internal
migrants from the country\'s peripheral areas.[^359] Despite an overall
decline of the country\'s total population, the proportion of the urban
demographic has consistently progressed from 47% in 2001 to 65% in
2023.`{{sfn|2023 Albanian census|2024|p=114}}`{=mediawiki}`{{sfn|2011 Albanian census|2012|p=10}}`{=mediawiki}[^360]
This sustained increase, coupled with the concentration in the
Tirana-Durrës region, has led to a spread of regional imbalances, with
the peripheral areas, particularly
[Dibër](Dibër_County "Dibër"){.wikilink} and
[Kukës](Kukës_County "Kukës"){.wikilink}, experiencing severe
depopulation.`{{sfn|Internal Migration Albania|2014|pp=12 & 18}}`{=mediawiki}`{{sfn|Internal Migration Albania|2014|p=15}}`{=mediawiki}`{{sfn|2023 Albanian census|2024|p=117}}`{=mediawiki}

```{=mediawiki}
{{Largest cities of Albania}}
```
```{=mediawiki}
{{Clear}}
```
### Language

```{=mediawiki}
{{Main|Languages of Albania}}
```
```{=mediawiki}
{{See also|Albanian language}}
```
```{=mediawiki}
{{update section|date=May 2023}}
```
![Founded in 1887, the
[Mësonjëtorja](Mësonjëtorja "Mësonjëtorja"){.wikilink} was the first
secular school to provide education in the
[Albanian](Albanian_language "Albanian"){.wikilink} during the Ottoman
Empire.](Mesonjetorja_e_Pare_Shqipe_ne_Korce.JPG "Founded in 1887, the Mësonjëtorja was the first secular school to provide education in the Albanian during the Ottoman Empire.")

The [official
language](official_language "official language"){.wikilink} of the
country is [Albanian](Albanian_language "Albanian"){.wikilink} which is
spoken by the vast majority of the country\'s population.[^361] Its
standard spoken and written form is revised and merged from the two main
dialects, [Gheg](Gheg "Gheg"){.wikilink} and
[Tosk](Tosk_Albanian "Tosk"){.wikilink}, though it is notably based more
on the Tosk dialect. The [Shkumbin](Shkumbin "Shkumbin"){.wikilink}
river is the rough dividing line between the two dialects. Among
minority languages, [Greek](Greek_language "Greek"){.wikilink} is the
second most-spoken language in the country, with 0.5 to 3% of the
population speaking it as first language, mainly in the country\'s south
where its speakers are concentrated.[^362][^363][^364][^365] Other
languages spoken by ethnic minorities in Albania include
[Aromanian](Aromanian_language "Aromanian"){.wikilink},
[Serbian](Serbian_language "Serbian"){.wikilink},
[Macedonian](Macedonian_language "Macedonian"){.wikilink},
[Bosnian](Bosnian_language "Bosnian"){.wikilink},
[Bulgarian](Bulgarian_language "Bulgarian"){.wikilink},
[Gorani](Gora_dialect "Gorani"){.wikilink}, and
[Roma](Romani_language "Roma"){.wikilink}.[^366] Macedonian is official
in the Pustec Municipality in East Albania. According to the 2011
population census, 2,765,610 or 98.8% of the population declared
[Albanian](Albanian_language "Albanian"){.wikilink} as their [mother
tongue](mother_tongue "mother tongue"){.wikilink}.[^367] Because of
large migration flows from Albania, over half of Albanians during their
life learn a second language. The main foreign language known is English
with 40.0%, followed by Italian with 27.8% and Greek with 22.9%. The
English speakers were mostly young people, the knowledge of Italian is
stable in every age group, while there is a decrease of the speakers of
Greek in the youngest group.[^368]

Among young people aged 25 or less, English, German and Turkish have
seen rising interest after 2000. Italian and French have had a stable
interest, while Greek has lost much of its previous interest. The trends
are linked with cultural and economic factors.[^369]

Young people have shown a growing interest in the [German
language](German_language "German language"){.wikilink} in recent
years.`{{Citation needed|date=June 2023}}`{=mediawiki} Some of them go
to Germany for studying or various experiences. Albania and Germany have
agreements for cooperating in helping young people of the two countries
know both cultures better.[^370] Due to a sharp rise in economic
relations with Turkey, interest in learning Turkish, in particular among
young people, has been growing on a yearly basis.[^371]

### Minorities

```{=mediawiki}
{{Main|Minorities of Albania}}
```
```{=mediawiki}
{{update section|date=September 2024}}
```
Designated national and cultural minorities in Albania include
Aromanian, Greek, Macedonian, Montenegrin, Serb, Roma, Egyptian, Bosnian
and Bulgarian peoples, as well as Gorani and Jews as other minority
groups.[^372][^373] The 2023 census recorded the ethnic composition as
[Albanians](Albanians "Albanians"){.wikilink} 2,186,917 (91,04% of the
total), [Greeks](Greeks_in_Albania "Greeks"){.wikilink} 23,485 (0,98%),
[Macedonians](Macedonians_of_Albania "Macedonians"){.wikilink} 2,281
(0,09%),
[Montenegrins](Montenegrins_of_Albania "Montenegrins"){.wikilink} 511
(0,02%), [Aromanians](Aromanians_in_Albania "Aromanians"){.wikilink}
2,459 (0,1%), [Roma](Romani_people_in_Albania "Roma"){.wikilink} 9,813
(0.4%), [Balkan
Egyptians](Balkan_Egyptians "Balkan Egyptians"){.wikilink} 12,375
(0,5%), [Bosnians](Bosniaks_in_Albania "Bosnians"){.wikilink} 2,963
(0,12%),
[Serbians](Serbs_and_Montenegrins_in_Albania "Serbians"){.wikilink} 584
(0,02%), [Bulgarians](Bulgarians_in_Albania "Bulgarians"){.wikilink}
7,057 (0,29%), mixed ethnicities 770 (0.03%), other ethnicities 3,798
(0.15%), and 134,451 (5.60%) with unspecified ethnicity, out of a total
population of
2,402,113.`{{sfn|2023 Albanian census|2024|p=75}}`{=mediawiki}

Contrary to official statistics that show an Albanian majority, the
minority groups have frequently disputed the official numbers, asserting
a higher percentage of the country\'s population. The Greek government
claimed there were an estimation of 300,000 ethnic Greeks in
Albania.[^374]`{{cite book|title=RFE/RL Research Report: Weekly Analyses from the RFE/RL Research Institute|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=RxgkAQAAIAAJ|year=1993|publisher=Radio Free Europe/Radio Liberty, Incorporated|quote=Albanian officials alleged that the priest was promoting irredentist sentiments among Albania's Greek minority&nbsp;– estimated at between 60,000 and 300,000.}}`{=mediawiki}

</ref>

[^375][^376][^377][^378] The [CIA World
Factbook](CIA_World_Factbook "CIA World Factbook"){.wikilink} estimates
the Greek minority to constitute 0.9%[^379] of the population. The US
State Department estimates that Greeks make up 1.17%, and other
minorities 0.23%, of the population.[^380] The latter questioned the
validity of the 2011 census data about the Greek minority, as
measurements had allegedly been affected by boycott.[^381]

```{=mediawiki}
{{multiple image
| align             = center
| total_width       = 600
| image_style       = border:none;

| caption1          = Regions with a traditional presence of ethnic groups other than Albanian.
| image2            = Albania majority ethnicity 2011 census.PNG
| caption2          = Distribution of ethnic groups within Albania, as of the 2011 census. Districts coloured grey are those where a majority of people did not declare an ethnicity (the question was optional). The census was criticised and boycotted by minorities in Albania.
| image3            = AlbaniaTraditionalCommunitiesByLanguageAndReligion.png
| caption3          = Traditional locations of linguistic and religious communities in Albania.
}}
```
