### Religion

```{=mediawiki}
{{Main|Religion in Albania}}
```
```{=mediawiki}
{{See also|Albanian paganism}}
```
```{=mediawiki}
{{Pie chart
| thumb = right
| caption = [[Religion in Albania]] as of the 2023 census conducted by the Instituti i Statistikës (INSTAT){{sfn|2023 Albanian census|2024|p=76}}
|label1 = [[Sunni Islam]]
|value1 = 45.86
|color1 = DarkGreen
|label2 = [[Roman Catholicism]]
|value2 = 8.38
|color2 = Gold
|label3 = [[Eastern Orthodoxy]]
|value3 = 7.22
|color3 = Red
|label4 = Evangelical Christians
|value4 = 0.4
|color4 = Skyblue
|label5 = [[Bektashi]]
|value5 = 4.81
|color5 = Yellowgreen
|label6 = Non-affiliated believers	
|value6 = 13.82
|color6 = Grey
|label7 = [[Atheism]]
|value7 = 3.55
|color7 = Lightgrey
|label8 = Undeclared	
|value8 = 15.76
|color8 = black
|label9 = Other	
|value9 = 0.15
|color9 = Pink
}}
```
Albania is a [secular](secular_state "secular"){.wikilink} and
religiously diverse country with no [official
religion](official_religion "official religion"){.wikilink}. [Freedom of
religion](Freedom_of_religion "Freedom of religion"){.wikilink},
[belief](freedom_of_belief "belief"){.wikilink} and
[conscience](Freedom_of_conscience "conscience"){.wikilink} are
guaranteed under the country\'s
[constitution](Constitution_of_Albania "constitution"){.wikilink}.[^382]
As of the 2023 Census, there were 1,101,718 (45.86%) [Sunni
Muslims](Sunni_Islam "Sunni Muslims"){.wikilink}, 201,530 (8.38%)
[Catholics](Roman_Catholicism "Catholics"){.wikilink}, 173,645 (7.22%)
[Eastern Orthodox](Eastern_Orthodoxy "Eastern Orthodox"){.wikilink},
115,644 (4.81%) [Bektashi
Muslims](Bektashi_Order "Bektashi Muslims"){.wikilink}, 9,658 (0.4%)
[Evangelicals](Evangelicalism "Evangelicals"){.wikilink}, 3,670 (0.15%)
of other religions, 332,155 (13.82%) believers without denomination,
85,311 (3.55%) Atheists and 378,782 (15.76%) did not provide an
answer.`{{sfn|2023 Albanian census|2024|p=76}}`{=mediawiki} Albania is
nevertheless ranked among the least religious countries in the
world.[^383] Religion constitute an important role in the lives of only
39% of the country\'s population.[^384] In another report, 56%
considered themselves religious, 30% considered themselves
non-religious, while 9% defined themselves as convinced atheists. 80%
believed in God.[^385]

The [Muslim Albanians](Islam_in_Albania "Muslim Albanians"){.wikilink}
are spread throughout the country.
[Orthodox](Orthodoxy_in_Albania "Orthodox"){.wikilink} and
[Bektashis](Bektashi "Bektashi"){.wikilink} are mostly found in the
south, whereas [Catholics](Catholicism_in_Albania "Catholic"){.wikilink}
mainly live in the north.[^386] In 2008, there were 694
[Catholic](Catholic "Catholic"){.wikilink} churches and 425
[orthodox](Eastern_Orthodox_Church "orthodox"){.wikilink} churches, 568
mosques and 70 [bektashi](Bektashi_Order "bektashi"){.wikilink}
[takyas](takya "takya"){.wikilink} in the country.[^387][^388]

![Representatives of the Sunni, Orthodox, Bektashi and Catholic Albanian
communities in
[Paris](Paris "Paris"){.wikilink}](Marche_Charlie_Hebdo_Paris_02.jpg "Representatives of the Sunni, Orthodox, Bektashi and Catholic Albanian communities in Paris")

During [modern times](Modern_history "modern times"){.wikilink}, the
Albanian republican, monarchic and later communist regimes followed a
systematic policy of separating religion from official functions and
cultural life. The country has never had an [official
religion](official_religion "official religion"){.wikilink} either as a
republic or as a kingdom. In the 20th century, the clergy of all faiths
was weakened under the monarchy and ultimately eradicated during the
1950s and 1960s, under the state policy of obliterating all organised
religion from the territories of Albania. The [communist
regime](Communism_in_Albania "communist regime"){.wikilink} persecuted
and suppressed religious observance and institutions and entirely
[banned religion](anti-religious "banned religion"){.wikilink}. The
country was then officially declared to be the world\'s first [atheist
state](atheist_state "atheist state"){.wikilink}. Religious freedom has
returned, however, since the [end of
communism](Fall_of_communism_in_Albania "end of communism"){.wikilink}.

Islam survived communist era persecution and reemerged in the modern era
as a practised religion in Albania.[^389] Some smaller Christian sects
in Albania include
[Evangelicals](Evangelicalism "Evangelicals"){.wikilink} and several
[Protestant](Protestant "Protestant"){.wikilink} communities including
[Seventh-day Adventist
Church](Seventh-day_Adventist_Church "Seventh-day Adventist Church"){.wikilink},
[Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day
Saints](The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints "Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints"){.wikilink}
and [Jehovah\'s
Witnesses](Jehovah's_Witnesses "Jehovah's Witnesses"){.wikilink}.[^390][^391][^392][^393]
The first recorded Protestant of Albania was Said Toptani, who travelled
around Europe and returned to [Tirana](Tirana "Tirana"){.wikilink} in
1853, where he preached
[Protestantism](Protestantism "Protestantism"){.wikilink}. The first
[evangelical
Protestants](evangelical_Protestants "evangelical Protestants"){.wikilink}
appeared in the 19th century and the Evangelical Alliance was founded in
1892. Nowadays, it has 160 member congregations from different
Protestant denominations. Following mass emigration to Israel after the
fall of communism, there are only 200 Albanian
[Jews](Judaism_in_Albania "Jews"){.wikilink} left in the
country.[^394][^395] `{{Clear}}`{=mediawiki}

## Culture

```{=mediawiki}
{{Main|Culture of Albania}}
```
### Symbols

```{=mediawiki}
{{Main|National symbols of Albania}}
```
![The [helmet](Arms_of_Skanderbeg "helmet"){.wikilink} of [Gjergj
Kastrioti
Skanderbeg](Skanderbeg "Gjergj Kastrioti Skanderbeg"){.wikilink} stands
as an emblem of Albanian
independence](Casque_Skanderbeg_Vienne.jpg "The helmet of Gjergj Kastrioti Skanderbeg stands as an emblem of Albanian independence")

The red and black [national
colours](national_colours "national colours"){.wikilink} are displayed
on the [flag of Albania](flag_of_Albania "flag of Albania"){.wikilink}
that is adorned with a [double-headed
eagle](double-headed_eagle "double-headed eagle"){.wikilink} as the
foremost recognised [national symbol of
Albania](National_symbols_of_Albania "national symbol of Albania"){.wikilink}.[^396][^397][^398]
With the black eagle portraying bravery and strength, the red field
symbolises the fortitude and sacrifices of the Albanian people.[^399]
The eagle is linked with the legacy of the national hero [Gjergj
Kastrioti](Skanderbeg "Gjergj Kastrioti"){.wikilink}, renowned as
Skanderbeg, who led a prosperous [resistance
movement](Skanderbeg's_rebellion "resistance movement"){.wikilink}
against Ottoman rule.[^400][^401][^402] Rooted in the Middle Ages, it
emerged as a [heraldic](Albanian_heraldry "heraldic"){.wikilink}
[symbol](Armorial_of_Albania "symbol"){.wikilink} in the [Principality
of Arbër](Principality_of_Arbanon "Principality of Arbër"){.wikilink}
and among notable Albanian dynasties such as the
[Dukagjini](Dukagjini_family "Dukagjini"){.wikilink},
[Kastrioti](Kastrioti_family "Kastrioti"){.wikilink},
[Muzaka](Muzaka_family "Muzaka"){.wikilink} and
[Thopia](Thopia_family "Thopia"){.wikilink} clans.[^403] Amid the
[Albanian
Renaissance](Albanian_National_Awakening "Albanian Renaissance"){.wikilink},
marking the resurgence of Albanian national identity and aspirations for
independence, the Albanian eagle regained its prominence.[^404] Its
importance reached its culmination with [Albania\'s declaration of
independence](Albanian_Declaration_of_Independence "Albania's declaration of independence"){.wikilink}
in 1912, when [Ismail Qemali](Ismail_Qemali "Ismail Qemali"){.wikilink}
raised it as the national flag in
[Vlorë](Vlorë "Vlorë"){.wikilink}.[^405]

The [coat of arms of
Albania](coat_of_arms_of_Albania "coat of arms of Albania"){.wikilink}
is an adaptation of the flag of Albania and the seal of
Skanderbeg.[^406] The coat comprises the black double-headed eagle
positioned at the centre of a red field.[^407] Above the eagle, it
carries the [helmet of
Skanderbeg](Arms_of_Skanderbeg "helmet of Skanderbeg"){.wikilink} that
is crowned with the head of a golden horned goat.[^408]
`{{lang|sq|[[Ti Shqipëri, më jep nder, më jep emrin Shqipëtar]]|i=no}}`{=mediawiki},
which translates to \"You Albania, give me honour, give me the name
Albanian\", is the [national motto of
Albania](List_of_national_mottos "national motto of Albania"){.wikilink}.[^409][^410]
It finds its foundation in the legacy of [national
poet](national_poet "national poet"){.wikilink} [Naim
Frashëri](Naim_Frashëri "Naim Frashëri"){.wikilink}, who held a renowned
role during the Albanian Renaissance.[^411] The [national anthem of
Albania](national_anthem "national anthem of Albania"){.wikilink},
\"`{{lang|sq|[[Himni i Flamurit]]|i=no}}`{=mediawiki}\", was composed by
[Asdreni](Aleksandër_Stavre_Drenova "Asdreni"){.wikilink} and adopted as
such following Albania\'s independence in 1912.[^412]

### Clothing

```{=mediawiki}
{{Main|Albanian national clothing|l1=Albanian traditional clothing}}
```
![The [Fustanella](Fustanella "Fustanella"){.wikilink} is designated as
the [national costume of
Albania](national_costume_of_Albania "national costume of Albania"){.wikilink}
with profound cultural significance within Albanian
culture](Les_Danseurs_Albanais_by_Alexandre-Gabriel_Decamps_(c._1835).jpg "The Fustanella is designated as the national costume of Albania with profound cultural significance within Albanian culture")

[Albanian traditional
clothing](Albanian_national_clothing "Albanian traditional clothing"){.wikilink},
with its contrasting variations for the northern
[Gheg](Ghegs "Gheg"){.wikilink} and southern [Tosk
Albanians](Tosks "Tosk Albanians"){.wikilink}, is a testament to
Albania\'s history, cultural diversity and ethnic identity.[^413] Gheg
men wear a light-colored shirt paired with wide loose-fitting trousers
referred to as the Tirq. These trousers are securely fastened by a wide
woven belt, the Brez. An integral component of their costume is the
[Xhamadan](Xhamadan "Xhamadan"){.wikilink}, a woolen red velvet vest
adorned with folkloric motifs and gold patterns.[^414] They also wear a
distinctive dome-shaped hat known as the
[Qeleshe](Qeleshe "Qeleshe"){.wikilink}, crafted from wool, with its
origins tracing back to the
[Illyrians](Illyrians "Illyrians"){.wikilink}.[^415][^416] Conversely,
Tosk men opt for the [Fustanella](Fustanella "Fustanella"){.wikilink}, a
knee-length garment designated as the national costume, typically white
with pleats, accompanied by a white shirt. They also wear a beige or
dark blue Xhamadan reminiscent of the Gheg attire. To complete their
attire, men wear knee-high socks referred to as
[Çorape](Çorape "Çorape"){.wikilink} and leather shoes known as
[Opinga](Opinga "Opinga"){.wikilink}.

The attire of Gheg and Tosk women is renowned for its rich palette of
colors and intricate filigree detailing, displayed across various
components including ear ornaments, finger rings, necklaces, belt
buckles and buttons. Key components include a long, light-toned shirt
paired with an apron, often accompanied by a woolen or felt mantle
referred to as the Xhoka. Additional upper garments, such as the Dollama
or Mintan, may be layered, along with a headscarf known as Kapica or
Shall. A distinctive variation incorporates a pair of aprons, including
the Pështjellak at the rear and the Paranik at the front. Integral to
the traditional attire of Gheg women is the ancient
[Xhubleta](Xhubleta "Xhubleta"){.wikilink}.[^417] Dedicated efforts have
been undertaken to preserve and promote the dress, acknowledging its
significance as an emblem of Albanian heritage.[^418] As a testament to
its importance, the Xhubleta has been inscribed on the
[UNESCO](UNESCO "UNESCO"){.wikilink} [Intangible Cultural Heritage
List](UNESCO_Intangible_Cultural_Heritage_Lists "Intangible Cultural Heritage List"){.wikilink}.[^419]
The distinctive bell-shaped garment is fashioned in black and enriched
with embroidered ethnic Albanian motifs, showcasing the remarkable
craftsmanship of northern Albania.[^420] Its crafting process involves
multiple intricate stages, encompassing the preparation of shajak fabric
and the precise cutting techniques.[^421] `{{Clear}}`{=mediawiki}

### Art and architecture {#art_and_architecture}

```{=mediawiki}
{{Main|Albanian art|Albanian architecture|l2=architecture}}
```
![[Butrint](Butrint "Butrint"){.wikilink} has been included in the
[UNESCO](UNESCO "UNESCO"){.wikilink} list of [World Heritage
Sites](World_Heritage_Site "World Heritage Site"){.wikilink} since
1992](Amphitheatre_of_Butrint_2009.jpg "Butrint has been included in the UNESCO list of World Heritage Sites since 1992")

The [artistic history](Albanian_art "artistic history"){.wikilink} of
Albania has been particularly influenced by a multitude of ancient and
medieval [people](Civilisation "people"){.wikilink}, traditions and
religions. It covers a broad spectrum with mediums and disciplines that
include painting, [pottery](pottery "pottery"){.wikilink}, sculpture,
[ceramics](ceramic "ceramic"){.wikilink} and architecture all of them
exemplifying a great variety in style and shape, in different regions
and period.

The rise of the [Byzantine](Byzantine_Empire "Byzantine"){.wikilink} and
[Ottoman Empire](Ottoman_Empire "Ottoman Empire"){.wikilink} in the
[Middle Ages](Middle_Ages "Middle Ages"){.wikilink} was accompanied by a
corresponding growth in
[Christian](Christian_art "Christian"){.wikilink} and [Islamic
art](Islamic_art "Islamic art"){.wikilink} in the lands of Albania which
are apparent in examples of architecture and mosaics throughout the
country.[^422] Centuries later, the [Albanian
Renaissance](Albanian_Renaissance "Albanian Renaissance"){.wikilink}
proved crucial to the emancipation of the modern Albanian culture and
saw unprecedented developments in all fields of literature and art
whereas artists sought to return to the ideals of
[Impressionism](Impressionism "Impressionism"){.wikilink} and
[Romanticism](Romanticism_(art) "Romanticism"){.wikilink}.[^423]
However, [Onufri](Onufri "Onufri"){.wikilink}, [Kolë
Idromeno](Kolë_Idromeno "Kolë Idromeno"){.wikilink}, [David
Selenica](David_Selenica "David Selenica"){.wikilink}, [Kostandin
Shpataraku](Kostandin_Shpataraku "Kostandin Shpataraku"){.wikilink} and
the [Zografi Brothers](Zografi_Brothers "Zografi Brothers"){.wikilink}
are the most eminent representatives of Albanian art.

The [architecture of
Albania](architecture_of_Albania "architecture of Albania"){.wikilink}
reflects the legacy of various civilisations tracing back to the
[classical
antiquity](classical_antiquity "classical antiquity"){.wikilink}. Major
cities in Albania have evolved from within the castle to include
dwellings, religious and commercial structures, with constant
redesigning of town squares and evolution of building techniques.
Nowadays, the cities and towns reflect a whole spectrum of various
[architectural
styles](architectural_style "architectural style"){.wikilink}. In the
20th century, many historical as well as
[sacred](Sacred_architecture "sacred"){.wikilink} buildings bearing the
ancient influence were demolished during the [communist
era](Communism_in_Albania "communist era"){.wikilink}.[^424]

[Ancient
architecture](Ancient_architecture "Ancient architecture"){.wikilink} is
found throughout Albania and most visible in
[Byllis](Byllis "Byllis"){.wikilink},
[Amantia](Amantia "Amantia"){.wikilink},
[Phoenice](Phoenice "Phoenice"){.wikilink},
[Apollonia](Apollonia_(Illyria) "Apollonia"){.wikilink},
[Butrint](Butrint "Butrint"){.wikilink},
[Antigonia](Antigonia_(Chaonia) "Antigonia"){.wikilink},
[Shkodër](Rozafa_Castle "Shkodër"){.wikilink} and
[Durrës](Durrës_Amphitheatre "Durrës"){.wikilink}. Considering the long
period of rule of the [Byzantine
Empire](Byzantine_Empire "Byzantine Empire"){.wikilink}, they introduced
castles, citadels, churches and monasteries with spectacular wealth of
visible [murals](mural "mural"){.wikilink} and
[frescos](fresco "fresco"){.wikilink}. Perhaps the best known examples
can be found in the southern Albanian cities and surroundings of
[Korçë](Korçë "Korçë"){.wikilink}, [Berat](Berat "Berat"){.wikilink},
[Voskopojë](Voskopojë "Voskopojë"){.wikilink} and
[Gjirokastër](Gjirokastër "Gjirokastër"){.wikilink}. Involving the
introduction of [Ottoman
architecture](Ottoman_architecture "Ottoman architecture"){.wikilink}
there was a development of mosques and other Islamic buildings,
particularly seen in Berat and Gjirokastër.

![*Bliss*, stainless steel sculpture by contemporary artist [Helidon
Xhixha](Helidon_Xhixha "Helidon Xhixha"){.wikilink}.](Bliss_by_Helidon_Xhixza.jpg "Bliss, stainless steel sculpture by contemporary artist Helidon Xhixha.")

A productive period of
[Historicism](Historicism_(art) "Historicism"){.wikilink}, [Art
Nouveau](Art_Nouveau "Art Nouveau"){.wikilink} and
[Neoclassicism](Neoclassicism "Neoclassicism"){.wikilink} merged into
the 19th century, best exemplified in [Korçë](Korçë "Korçë"){.wikilink}.
The 20th century brought new architectural styles such as the modern
[Italian style](Italianate_architecture "Italian style"){.wikilink},
which is present in [Tirana](Tirana "Tirana"){.wikilink} such as the
[Skanderbeg Square](Skanderbeg_Square "Skanderbeg Square"){.wikilink}
and Ministries. It is also present in Shkodër,
[Vlorë](Vlorë "Vlorë"){.wikilink},
[Sarandë](Sarandë "Sarandë"){.wikilink} and
[Durrës](Durrës "Durrës"){.wikilink}. Moreover, other towns received
their present-day Albania-unique appearance through various cultural or
economic influences.

[Socialist
classicism](Socialist_classicism "Socialist classicism"){.wikilink}
arrived during the [communist
era](Peoples_Republic_of_Albania "communist era"){.wikilink} in Albania
after the [Second World
War](Second_World_War "Second World War"){.wikilink}. At this period
many socialist-styled complexes, wide roads and factories were
constructed, while town squares were redesigned and numerous of historic
and important buildings demolished. Notable examples of that style
include the [Mother Teresa
Square](Mother_Teresa_Square_(Tirana) "Mother Teresa Square"){.wikilink},
[Pyramid of Tirana](Pyramid_of_Tirana "Pyramid of Tirana"){.wikilink},
[Palace of
Congresses](Palace_of_Congresses "Palace of Congresses"){.wikilink} and
so on.

Three Albanian [archaeological](Archaeology "archaeological"){.wikilink}
sites are included in the list of [UNESCO World Heritage
Sites](UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site "UNESCO World Heritage Site"){.wikilink}.
These include the ancient remains of Butrint, the medieval [Historic
Centres of Berat and
Gjirokastër](Historic_Centres_of_Berat_and_Gjirokastër "Historic Centres of Berat and Gjirokastër"){.wikilink},
and [Natural and Cultural Heritage of the Ohrid
region](Ohrid_Lake "Natural and Cultural Heritage of the Ohrid region"){.wikilink}
site shared with [North
Macedonia](North_Macedonia "North Macedonia"){.wikilink} since
2019.[^425][^426] Furthermore, the royal [Illyrian
tombs](Royal_Tombs_of_Selca_e_Poshtme "Illyrian tombs"){.wikilink}, the
remains of [Apollonia](Apollonia_(Illyria) "Apollonia"){.wikilink}, the
ancient [Amphitheatre](Durrës_Amphitheatre "Amphitheatre"){.wikilink} of
Durrës and the [Fortress of
Bashtovë](Fortress_of_Bashtovë "Fortress of Bashtovë"){.wikilink} has
been included on the tentative list of Albania.

### Cuisine

```{=mediawiki}
{{Main|Albanian cuisine}}
```
![Bukë misri ([cornbread](cornbread "cornbread"){.wikilink}) is a staple
on the Albanian
table](Bukë_kollomoqe,_bukë_misri.JPG "Bukë misri (cornbread) is a staple on the Albanian table")

Throughout the centuries, [Albanian
cuisine](Albanian_cuisine "Albanian cuisine"){.wikilink} has been widely
influenced by [Albanian
culture](Albanian_culture "Albanian culture"){.wikilink},
[geography](Geography_of_Albania "geography"){.wikilink} and
[history](History_of_Albania "history"){.wikilink}, and as such,
different parts of the country enjoy specific [regional
cuisines](regional_cuisine "regional cuisine"){.wikilink}. Cooking
traditions especially vary between the north and the south, owing to
differing [topography](topography "topography"){.wikilink} and
[climate](climate "climate"){.wikilink} that essentially contribute to
the excellent growth conditions for a wide array of herbs, fruits, and
vegetables.[^427]

Albanians produce and use many varieties of fruits such as
[lemons](Lemon_(fruit) "lemon"){.wikilink}, oranges,
[figs](Figs_(fruit) "fig"){.wikilink}, and most notably,
[olives](Olive_(fruit) "olive"){.wikilink}, which are perhaps the most
important element of Albanian cooking. Spices and other herbs such as
[basil](Basil_(herb) "basil"){.wikilink},
[lavender](lavender "lavender"){.wikilink},
[mint](Spearmint "mint"){.wikilink},
[oregano](oregano "oregano"){.wikilink},
[rosemary](rosemary "rosemary"){.wikilink}, and
[thyme](thyme "thyme"){.wikilink} are widely used, as are vegetables
such as garlic, onions, [peppers](Bell_pepper "pepper"){.wikilink},
potatoes, tomatoes, as well as [legumes](legume "legume"){.wikilink} of
all types.

With a coastline along the
[Adriatic](Albanian_Adriatic_Sea_Coast "Adriatic"){.wikilink} and
[Ionian](Albanian_Ionian_Sea_Coast "Ionian"){.wikilink} in the
[Mediterranean Sea](Mediterranean_Sea "Mediterranean Sea"){.wikilink},
fish, [crustaceans](crustacean "crustacean"){.wikilink}, and seafood are
a popular and an integral part of the Albanian diet. Otherwise,
[lamb](Lamb_(food) "lamb"){.wikilink} is the traditional meat for
different holidays and [religious
festivals](religious_festival "religious festival"){.wikilink} for both
[Christians](Christianity_in_Albania "Christians"){.wikilink} and
[Muslims](Islam_in_Albania "Muslim"){.wikilink}, although poultry, beef,
and pork are also in plentiful supply.

![Speca të fërguar (roasted [peppers](Capsicum "pepper"){.wikilink})
served with [pite](Pite_(food) "pite"){.wikilink}, a traditional and
prominent layered Albanian
pie](Albanian_cuisine_-_Pite_dhe_Speca.jpg "Speca të fërguar (roasted peppers) served with pite, a traditional and prominent layered Albanian pie")

[Tavë kosi](Tavë_kosi "Tavë kosi"){.wikilink} (\"[soured
milk](soured_milk "soured milk"){.wikilink}
[casserole](casserole "casserole"){.wikilink}\") is the [national
dish](national_dish "national dish"){.wikilink} of Albania, consisting
of lamb and rice baked under a thick, tart veil of
[yoghurt](yoghurt "yoghurt"){.wikilink}.
[Fërgesë](Fërgesë "Fërgesë"){.wikilink} is another national dish, made
up of peppers, tomatoes, and [cottage
cheese](cottage_cheese "cottage cheese"){.wikilink}. Pite is also
popular, a baked pastry with a filling of a mixture of
[spinach](spinach "spinach"){.wikilink} and gjizë (curd) or mish
([ground meat](ground_meat "ground meat"){.wikilink}).

Petulla, a traditional fried dough, is also a popular speciality, and is
served with [powdered sugar](powdered_sugar "powdered sugar"){.wikilink}
or [feta cheese](feta_cheese "feta cheese"){.wikilink} and different
sorts of [fruit jams](Fruit_preserves "fruit jam"){.wikilink}.
[Flia](Flia "Flia"){.wikilink} consists of multiple
[crêpe](crêpe "crêpe"){.wikilink}-like layers brushed with cream and
served with sour cream. [Krofne](Krofne "Krofne"){.wikilink}, similar to
[Berliner
doughnuts](Berliner_(doughnut) "Berliner doughnuts"){.wikilink}, are
filled with jam, or chocolate and often eaten during winter.

Coffee is an integral part of the Albanian lifestyle. The country has
more coffee houses per capita than any other country in the world.[^428]
Tea is also enjoyed both at home or outside at cafés, bars, or
restaurants. Çaj Mali ([Sideritis](Sideritis "Sideritis"){.wikilink}
tea) is enormously beloved, and a part of the daily routine for most
Albanians. It is cultivated across Southern Albania and noted for its
medicinal properties. [Black tea](Black_tea "Black tea"){.wikilink} is
also popular.

[Albanian wine](Albanian_wine "Albanian wine"){.wikilink} is also common
throughout the country, and has been cultivated for thousands of years.
Albania has a long and ancient history of wine production, and belongs
to the [Old World of wine producing
countries](Old_World_wine "Old World of wine producing countries"){.wikilink}.[^429][^430]

```{=mediawiki}
{{Clear}}
```
### Music

```{=mediawiki}
{{Main|Music of Albania}}
```
```{=mediawiki}
{{See also|Albanian war dances}}
```
![[Albanian
iso-polyphony](Albanian_iso-polyphony "Albanian iso-polyphony"){.wikilink}
is designated as an [UNESCO](UNESCO "UNESCO"){.wikilink} [Masterpiece of
the Oral and Intangible Heritage of
Humanity](Masterpieces_of_the_Oral_and_Intangible_Heritage_of_Humanity "Masterpiece of the Oral and Intangible Heritage of Humanity"){.wikilink}.[^431]](A_traditional_male_folk_group_from_Skrapar.JPG "Albanian iso-polyphony is designated as an UNESCO Masterpiece of the Oral and Intangible Heritage of Humanity.")

Albanian folk music is a prominent part of the national identity, and
continues to play a major part in overall [Albanian
music](Music_of_Albania "Albanian music"){.wikilink}. Folk music can be
divided into two stylistic groups, mainly the northern
[Gheg](Gheg_Albanian "Gheg"){.wikilink} varieties, and southern
[Lab](Labëria "Lab"){.wikilink} and
[Tosk](Tosk_Albanian "Tosk"){.wikilink} varieties. Northern and southern
traditions are contrasted by a rugged tone from the north, and the more
relaxed southern form of music.

Many songs concern events from [Albanian
history](History_of_Albania "Albanian history"){.wikilink} and
[culture](Culture_of_Albania "culture"){.wikilink}, including
traditional themes of honour, hospitality, treachery, and revenge. The
first compilation of Albanian folk music was made by two
[Himariot](Himara "Himariot"){.wikilink} musicians, [Neço
Muka](Neço_Muko "Neço Muka"){.wikilink} and Koço Çakali, in Paris,
during their work with Albanian soprano [Tefta
Tashko-Koço](Tefta_Tashko-Koço "Tefta Tashko-Koço"){.wikilink}. Several
[gramophone](Phonograph_record "gramophone"){.wikilink} compilations
were recorded at the time by the three artists, which eventually led to
the recognition of [Albanian
iso-polyphony](Albanian_iso-polyphony "Albanian iso-polyphony"){.wikilink}
as a [UNESCO](UNESCO "UNESCO"){.wikilink} [Intangible Cultural
Heritage](UNESCO_Intangible_Cultural_Heritage_Lists "Intangible Cultural Heritage"){.wikilink}.[^433]

```{=mediawiki}
{{lang|sq|[[Festivali i Këngës]]|italic=no}}
```
is a traditional Albanian song contest organised by the national
broadcaster
`{{lang|sq|[[Radio Televizioni Shqiptar]]|italic=no}}`{=mediawiki}
(RTSH). The festival is celebrated annually since its inauguration in
1962 and has launched the careers of some of Albania\'s most successful
singers including [Vaçe Zela](Vaçe_Zela "Vaçe Zela"){.wikilink} and
[Parashqevi
Simaku](Parashqevi_Simaku "Parashqevi Simaku"){.wikilink}.[^434] It is
significantly a music competition among Albanian performers presenting
unreleased songs in premiere, composed by Albanian authors and voted by
juries or by public.

Contemporary artists [Rita Ora](Rita_Ora "Rita Ora"){.wikilink}, [Bebe
Rexha](Bebe_Rexha "Bebe Rexha"){.wikilink}, [Era
Istrefi](Era_Istrefi "Era Istrefi"){.wikilink}, [Dua
Lipa](Dua_Lipa "Dua Lipa"){.wikilink}, [Ava
Max](Ava_Max "Ava Max"){.wikilink},
[Bleona](Bleona "Bleona"){.wikilink}, [Elvana
Gjata](Elvana_Gjata "Elvana Gjata"){.wikilink}, [Ermonela
Jaho](Ermonela_Jaho "Ermonela Jaho"){.wikilink}, and [Inva
Mula](Inva_Mula "Inva Mula"){.wikilink} have achieved international
recognition for their music,[^435] while soprano [Ermonela
Jaho](Ermonela_Jaho "Ermonela Jaho"){.wikilink} has been described by
some as the \"world\'s most acclaimed soprano\".[^436] Albanian opera
singer [Saimir Pirgu](Saimir_Pirgu "Saimir Pirgu"){.wikilink} was
nominated for the 2017 [Grammy
Award](Grammy_Award "Grammy Award"){.wikilink}.[^437]

### Literature

```{=mediawiki}
{{More citations needed section|date=October 2018}}
```
```{=mediawiki}
{{Main|Albanian literature}}
```
![An excerpt from the [Meshari](Meshari "Meshari"){.wikilink} *(The
Missal)* written by [Gjon Buzuku](Gjon_Buzuku "Gjon Buzuku"){.wikilink}
`<small>`{=html}(1555)`</small>`{=html}](Meshari.jpg "An excerpt from the Meshari (The Missal) written by Gjon Buzuku (1555)")

The cultural renaissance was first of all expressed through the
development of the [Albanian
language](Albanian_language "Albanian language"){.wikilink} in the area
of church texts and publications. The Protestant reforms invigorated
hopes for the development of the local language and literary tradition,
when cleric [Gjon Buzuku](Gjon_Buzuku "Gjon Buzuku"){.wikilink}
translated the [Catholic
liturgy](Catholic_liturgy "Catholic liturgy"){.wikilink} into Albanian,
trying to do for Albanian what [Martin
Luther](Martin_Luther "Martin Luther"){.wikilink} had done for German.
[Meshari](Meshari "Meshari"){.wikilink} (*The Missal*) written by [Gjon
Buzuku](Gjon_Buzuku "Gjon Buzuku"){.wikilink} was published in 1555 and
is considered one of the first literary work of written Albanian during
the Middle Ages. The refined level of the language and the stabilised
orthography must be the result of an earlier tradition of written
Albanian, a tradition that is not well understood. However, there is
some fragmented evidence, pre-dating Buzuku, which indicates that
Albanian was written from at least the 14th century.

![[Parashqevi
Qiriazi](Parashqevi_Qiriazi "Parashqevi Qiriazi"){.wikilink} -- teacher
and feminist
(1880--1970)](Parashqevi-qirjazi_152_186.jpg "Parashqevi Qiriazi – teacher and feminist (1880–1970)")

Albanian writings from these centuries must not have been religious
texts only, but historical chronicles too. They are mentioned by the
humanist [Marin Barleti](Marin_Barleti "Marin Barleti"){.wikilink}, who
in his book [Siege of
Shkodër](Siege_of_Shkodra_(1478)#The_Book "Siege of Shkodër"){.wikilink}
(*Rrethimi i Shkodrës*) from 1504, confirms that he leafed through such
chronicles written in the language of the people (*in vernacula lingua*)
as well as his famous biography of
[Skanderbeg](Skanderbeg "Skanderbeg"){.wikilink} [Historia de vita et
gestis Scanderbegi Epirotarum
principis](Marin_Barleti "Historia de vita et gestis Scanderbegi Epirotarum principis"){.wikilink}
(*History of Skanderbeg*) from 1508. The *History of Skanderbeg* is
still the foundation of Skanderbeg studies and is considered an Albanian
cultural treasure, vital to the formation of Albanian national
self-consciousness.

During the 16th and the 17th centuries, the
[catechism](catechism "catechism"){.wikilink} (*E mbësuame krishterë*)
(Christian Teachings) from 1592 written by [Lekë
Matrënga](Lekë_Matrënga "Lekë Matrënga"){.wikilink}, (*Doktrina e
krishterë*) (The Christian Doctrine) from 1618 and (*Rituale romanum*)
1621 by [Pjetër Budi](Pjetër_Budi "Pjetër Budi"){.wikilink}, the first
writer of original Albanian [prose](prose "prose"){.wikilink} and
poetry, an [apology](Remorse "apology"){.wikilink} for George Castriot
(1636) by [Frang Bardhi](Frang_Bardhi "Frang Bardhi"){.wikilink}, who
also published a dictionary and
[folklore](folklore "folklore"){.wikilink} creations, the
theological-philosophical treaty *[Cuneus
Prophetarum](Cuneus_Prophetarum "Cuneus Prophetarum"){.wikilink}* (The
Band of Prophets) (1685) by [Pjetër
Bogdani](Pjetër_Bogdani "Pjetër Bogdani"){.wikilink}, the most universal
personality of Albanian [Middle
Ages](Middle_Ages "Middle Ages"){.wikilink}, were published in
[Albanian](Albanian_language "Albanian"){.wikilink}. The most famous
Albanian writer in the 20th and 21st century is probably [Ismail
Kadare](Ismail_Kadare "Ismail Kadare"){.wikilink}.

### Sports

```{=mediawiki}
{{See also|Albania at the Olympics|Albania at the Mediterranean Games}}
```
Albania participated at the [Olympic Games in
1972](1972_Summer_Olympics "Olympic Games in 1972"){.wikilink} for the
first time. The country made their Winter Olympic Games debut in
[2006](Winter_Olympics_2006 "2006"){.wikilink}. Albania missed the next
four games, two of them due to the 1980 and 1984 boycotts, but returned
for the 1992 games in
[Barcelona](1992_Olympic_Winter_Games "Barcelona"){.wikilink}. Since
then, Albania have participated in all games. Albania normally competes
in events that include swimming, athletics, weightlifting, shooting and
wrestling. The country have been represented by the [National Olympic
Committee of
Albania](National_Olympic_Committee_of_Albania "National Olympic Committee of Albania"){.wikilink}
since 1972. The nation has participated at the [Mediterranean
Games](Mediterranean_Games "Mediterranean Games"){.wikilink} since the
games of [1987](1987_Mediterranean_Games "1987"){.wikilink} in Syria.
The Albanian athletes have won a total of 43 (8 gold, 17 silver and 18
bronze) medals from [1987](1987_Mediterranean_Games "1987"){.wikilink}
to [2013](2013_Mediterranean_Games "2013"){.wikilink}.

![[Arena Kombëtare](Arena_Kombëtare "Arena Kombëtare"){.wikilink} in
central
Tirana](Muzeu_Arkeologjike_Tirane.jpg "Arena Kombëtare in central Tirana")

Popular sports in Albania include
[football](Football_in_Albania "football"){.wikilink}, weightlifting,
[basketball](Albania_national_basketball_team "basketball"){.wikilink},
volleyball, tennis, swimming, [rugby
union](rugby_union "rugby union"){.wikilink} and gymnastics. Football is
by far the most popular sport in Albania. It is governed by the
[Football Association of
Albania](Football_Association_of_Albania "Football Association of Albania"){.wikilink}
(`{{langx|sq|Federata Shqiptare e Futbollit}}`{=mediawiki}, F.SH.F.),
which has membership in [FIFA](FIFA "FIFA"){.wikilink} and
[UEFA](UEFA "UEFA"){.wikilink}.

The [Albania national football
team](Albania_national_football_team "Albania national football team"){.wikilink},
ranking 51st in the [World](FIFA_World_Rankings "World"){.wikilink} in
2017 (highest 22nd on 22 August 2015) have won the [1946 Balkan
Cup](1946_Balkan_Cup "1946 Balkan Cup"){.wikilink} and the [Malta
Rothmans International Tournament
2000](Rothmans_International_Tournament_2000 "Malta Rothmans International Tournament 2000"){.wikilink},
but had never participated in any major [UEFA](UEFA "UEFA"){.wikilink}
or [FIFA](FIFA "FIFA"){.wikilink} tournament, until [UEFA Euro
2016](UEFA_Euro_2016 "UEFA Euro 2016"){.wikilink}, Albania\'s first ever
appearance at the continental tournament and at a major men\'s football
tournament. Albania scored their first ever goal in a major tournament
and secured their first ever win in European Championship when they beat
[Romania](Romania_national_football_team "Romania"){.wikilink} by 1--0
in a [UEFA Euro 2016](UEFA_Euro_2016 "UEFA Euro 2016"){.wikilink} match
on 19 June 2016.[^438][^439] The most successful football clubs are
[Skënderbeu](KF_Skënderbeu_Korçë "Skënderbeu"){.wikilink}, [KF
Tirana](KF_Tirana "KF Tirana"){.wikilink}, [Dinamo
Tirana](FK_Dinamo_Tirana "Dinamo Tirana"){.wikilink},
[Partizani](FK_Partizani_Tirana "Partizani"){.wikilink} and
[Vllaznia](KF_Vllaznia_Shkodër "Vllaznia"){.wikilink}.

Weightlifting is one of the most successful individual sport for the
Albanians, with the national team winning medals at the [European
Weightlifting
Championships](European_Weightlifting_Championships "European Weightlifting Championships"){.wikilink}
and the rest international competitions. Albanian weightlifters have won
a total of 16 medals at the [European
Championships](European_Weightlifting_Championships "European Championships"){.wikilink}
with 1 of them being gold, 7 silver and 8 bronze. In the [World
Weightlifting
Championships](World_Weightlifting_Championships "World Weightlifting Championships"){.wikilink},
the Albanian weightlifting team has won in
[1972](1972_World_Weightlifting_Championships "1972"){.wikilink} a gold
in [2002](2002_World_Weightlifting_Championships "2002"){.wikilink} a
silver and in
[2011](2011_World_Weightlifting_Championships "2011"){.wikilink} a
bronze medal.

## Human rights {#human_rights}

![2016 LGBT+ Pride in
[Tirana](Tirana "Tirana"){.wikilink}.](Tirana_Gay(P)Ride_2016.jpg "2016 LGBT+ Pride in Tirana.")

Nearly 60% of women in rural areas suffer physical or psychological
violence and nearly 8% are victims of sexual violence. Protection orders
are often violated. In 2014 the Albanian Helsinki Committee (AHC)
reported that the number of female murder victims is still high.[^440]
The Commissioner for Protection from Discrimination has raised concerns
regarding the family registration law that discriminates against women.
As a result, heads of households, who are overwhelmingly men, have the
right to change family residency without their partners\'
permission.[^441]

In 2015, the association
[ILGA-Europe](ILGA-Europe "ILGA-Europe"){.wikilink} ranked Albania 19th
in terms of LGBT rights out of 49 observed European countries.[^442]
Meanwhile, on the latest report in 2022, lack of progress caused Albania
to be ranked the 28th country in Europe, among 49 countries
observed.[^443]

    refugees](Albanian_diaspora "Albanian refugees"){.wikilink}
    emigrated to [Italy](Albanians_in_Italy "Italy"){.wikilink},
    [Greece](Albanian_communities_in_Greece "Greece"){.wikilink},
    [Switzerland](Albanians_in_Switzerland "Switzerland"){.wikilink},
    [Germany](Albanians_in_Germany "Germany"){.wikilink}, or North
    America.
